Questions and Answers Between a Japanese Reporter and Rose 28

Saying that Japan can understand that Britain will not act alone

(Tokyo) The questions and answers between Lees-Rose and the press corps are roughly as follows:

Reporter: You strongly advocate for cooperation between Britain and Japan in China. However, does Britain intend to cooperate with Japan on trade issues in countries other than China?

Rose: The issue of cooperation between Britain and Japan on trade issues in countries other than China was discussed at the Anglo-Japanese consultations the year before last. In my opinion, the reason why Japanese goods are hindered from entering countries other than Britain is overproduction. To alleviate this situation, it is necessary to eliminate useless competition. Japan itself also needs to reflect on this.

Reporter: When competition is eliminated, if countries with vast territories and abundant resources like Britain benefit, countries with small territories and scarce resources like Japan will be at a great disadvantage. In this situation, does Britain have any plans to provide convenience to Japan?

Rose: This question is incomprehensible. Although Japan's resources are scarce, it can purchase raw materials cheaply from foreign countries. Therefore, if Japan wants to overcome the current difficulties, it should restrict production and raise prices. Britain intends to implement competition not only in China, but also in any situation based on mutual agreement.

Reporter: What are your views on Japan's special position in the East?

Rose: Japan is a stabilizing force in the East and bears a major responsibility.

Reporter: The authorities believe that it is too early to implement economic aid to China at present, and that a political solution is a prerequisite. During your visit to Japan this time, you suggested to the Japanese government the need for investment in Chinese railways and the rectification of interests in North China, giving us the impression that you are acting as an advocate for the Chinese government. However, according to the Japanese government, you should advise the Chinese government to correct its attitude towards Japan, which would contribute significantly to opening up Sino-Japanese relations. What are your thoughts on this?

Rose: I am not an advocate for the Chinese government. I am only inspecting China for my own purposes. You urge me to advise the Chinese government, but I am an economic expert and do not want to interfere in political issues. Also, Japan currently has the opinion of eradicating the Chinese Communist Party. The Chinese people in the interior are living in difficult conditions, which is why the Communist Party exists. To eradicate the Chinese Communist Party, it is necessary to stabilize the lives of its people. Building railways in China and improving the living conditions of farmers will make it possible to export Japanese goods and benefit Japanese industrialists.

Reporter: Which areas in China are targeted for railway construction?

Rose: China is the country with the fewest railways in the world, so railways should be built everywhere.

Reporter: It is heard that the Japanese government will provide aid to China with materials. Has a concrete plan been obtained for this?

Rose: A concrete plan has not yet been decided, but I am pleased to hear that the Japanese government has this intention.

Reporter: If Japan is unwilling to provide joint aid to China, will Britain provide aid alone? If aid is provided alone, what will be the extent of it?

Rose: Since the Japanese government has already expressed its intention to provide joint aid to China, I believe that this kind of problem will not occur at present.

Reporter: Does the Japanese government have any concrete proposals for the construction of railways in China and the reorganization of the central bank?

Rose: When improving China's external credit, it is not possible to propose these concrete plans. From the perspective of this improvement in external credit, China's tariff issue has great significance. There should be a clear description of this matter. As for the reorganization of the central bank, I have also made considerable efforts. The Chinese authorities are also working hard on this, but the specific results are unknown.

Reporter: Then what is the main goal of the central bank's reorganization?

Rose: Its organization is intended to emulate the Bank of Japan, thereby promoting it.

Reporter: What are your views on the new Sino-US agreement recently concluded in Washington?

Rose: The case has not been formally announced, so its content is unknown, but it is undoubtedly beneficial to China. However, this matter has nothing to do with Britain.

Reporter: It is said that the increase or decrease in China's tariff revenue has great significance for China's revival, but I don't know how to solve this problem. To solve this problem, what kind of assistance from Japan is considered necessary?

Rose: The decrease in China's tariff revenue is mainly due to fluctuations in silver prices and "special trade" in North China. However, this solution is a political issue, and I am not in a position to express my opinion, etc. (Kyodo News Agency dispatch, 13th)

The Situation of the US Presidential Election: Roosevelt Can Be Re-elected; The Republican Party Nominated Knox as the Vice-Presidential Candidate; Borah Disagrees with Landon's Financial Policy

(Washington) Although Kansas Governor Landon and Chicago newspaper publisher Knox have been selected as the Republican candidates for President and Vice President, incumbent President Roosevelt still has the upper hand in the presidential election campaign. Neutral observers believe that the election of Landon and Knox will not seriously jeopardize Roosevelt's chances. The betting odds on Roosevelt's election on Wall Street are eight to five. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

Cleveland: The Republican National Convention today unanimously nominated Chicago publisher Knox as the Vice-Presidential candidate, with 1,003 delegates in attendance. (National News Agency dispatch, 12th)

Cleveland: The selection of Landon and Knox as the Republican candidates for President and Vice President is largely due to William Hearst's newspapers. Landon relied on Hearst's newspapers across the country to promote him, rising from an obscure state politician to a national figure. Knox is famous for handling the sales affairs of Hearst's newspapers. The delegates to the convention are now returning home, and everyone wants to ask, "What about Borah?" Borah, after Landon telegraphed the convention, stating that after stabilizing the currency, his determination to leave the party has become stronger. When he arrived in Washington, he refused to announce whether he supported Landon, saying only that he did not know what Landon's words on gold meant. If he intends to restore the gold standard, then his political views are completely different. Borah also said that he had no objection to Knox's election as the Vice-Presidential candidate. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

(Washington) Experts here believe that the Republican campaign platform clearly does not include the Far East issue, which proves that the party does not want to get involved in the Far East vortex. The platform is silent on the Open Door Policy, the silver issue, and the Philippine issues, which shows that the party is now paying attention to domestic issues, and its enthusiasm for the Far East is not as strong as before. Those familiar with the Far East issue are surprised that the party's campaign platform failed to directly or indirectly mention the Open Door Policy. The platform also does not have a single word of criticism about the government's silver purchase program. According to observers familiar with current affairs, the reason why the silver issue was not mentioned is obviously due to Senator Borah's opposition. The party was quite unsure of what to do with the silver issue when drafting the platform, because supporting the silver purchase policy would harm the interests of hard money advocates in the eastern states, and opposing it would incur the displeasure of the mining areas in the western valley states. Regarding the issue of currency stabilization, the party has little understanding of the currencies of China and Japan, and its wording is empty and unimportant. Regarding the navy and army, the platform only has the phrase "strengthening military power," so the party has little clear expression on this issue. The phrase in the platform protecting the domestic market from the dumping of cheap goods naturally includes Japan, but because the wording is vague, there is no anti-Japanese sentiment. (National News Agency dispatch, 12th)

Ogden: The chairman of the National Veterans Association, Sanders, declared today that the National Veterans Republican Party platform ignores the Red Menace, so it cannot be endorsed, and said that the platform should include an article stating that recognition of the Soviet Union will be withdrawn if the Soviet Union continues to propagate communism in the United States. (National News Agency dispatch, 12th)

Dallas: President Roosevelt also said today that he will take avoiding foreign disputes and curbing commercial monopolies as the government's policy direction. He firmly guarantees that the United States will not be involved in the vortex of European and Asian disputes. The United States hopes to assist international undertakings, thereby serving as a standard for unity, cooperation, and friendship, but this assistance is only of a moral nature. This afternoon, the President also spoke at the Cotton Exchange here, saying that if monopolies are not curbed, the United States will only have hotels and no families. I oppose the concentration of wealth in the hands of a few people, so I firmly declare that I will vigorously maintain the interests of small businesses and workers. The result of a few people controlling economic power will make labor a commodity. If we tolerate this fact, we will abandon the freedom given by history. What we need is not hotels but families. We have now democratized politics, and in the future, we will democratize opportunities. (National News Agency dispatch, 12th)

Dallas: President Roosevelt recently delivered a speech at the "Centennial Celebration of Texas's Admission to the United States," which has been recorded in another dispatch. Here is a supplement: He said, "We in the United States have promoted national ideas and also promoted international ideas, and we should maintain a peaceful situation." Although the United States is willing to encourage all countries in the world to pursue a good neighborly and sincere foreign policy, it should clearly tell all countries that in the event of danger in the future, the United States can only provide assistance in spirit." (Havas dispatch, 12th)

Cleveland: Knox has now been nominated as the Republican candidate for Vice President of the United States. He initially ran a small newspaper in Michigan, famous for criticizing corruption, and then appeared in politics, with unhindered eloquence. To this day, he has devoted himself to the newspaper industry. Since Roosevelt took office, he has written articles criticizing him with all his might, even believing that Roosevelt's policies endanger the American political system. In September of last year, the Illinois Republican State Committee approved his participation in the presidential race, and at the same time, he won the majority of votes in the state's primary election. (National News Agency dispatch, 13th)

Anglo-Russian Naval Conference: Russia Did Not Demand Equal Rights

(London) Regarding the Anglo-Russian naval talks, it was rumored that Britain had in principle recognized that the Soviet Navy in the Pacific should be on an equal footing with the Japanese Navy. Officials here solemnly denied this. Naval figures also said that this news is incomprehensible, because the agreement to be established between Britain and Russia is purely a qualitative restriction method. Regarding this, the Soviet Union did not demand equal rights. What it demanded was that if Japan does not accept the existing naval treaties of Britain, the United States, and France for one day, then the Soviet Union will not abide by the qualitative restriction methods stipulated in these treaties for one day, and will reserve the right to build a fleet in the Pacific. Naval figures also said that the future naval agreement between Britain and Russia will be issued in the form of an exchange of letters. Its content is that if Japan does not violate the existing naval treaties of Britain, the United States, and France, then the Soviet Union will naturally abide by the future naval agreement between Britain and Russia. (Havas, 13th)

British Destroyer Increase Plan: The United States Advocates Using the Escalator Clause

(London) In May, the British government sent a memorandum to the signatory countries of the London Naval Treaty (1920), namely the United States and Japan, requesting that the country's total destroyer tonnage still be set at 190,000 tons (the Sea Treaty stipulated 150,000 tons). As for the 10,000-ton cruisers, there are a total of four that should be destroyed according to the treaty. The country also requested that one of them be converted into a training ship, and the other three be converted into Class B cruisers, which would still be allowed to be retained. The United States government immediately submitted an answer, stating that the country does not oppose this request in principle, but as far as the London Sea Treaty is concerned, Britain should invoke Article 21 of the treaty, namely the "Escalator Clause." The Japanese government recently submitted a verbal answer through its chargé d'affaires, Fujii, and notified Britain of the total tonnage of destroyers and submarines that the country should destroy in accordance with the treaty but wanted to retain. Well-informed sources believe that if Britain had adopted the answer proposed by the United States at that time, that is, implemented the escalator clause, then the situation of this case would definitely have been changed, that is, Japan would have no reason to make equivalent demands. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

German University of Frankfurt: Opening of the Chinese Academy

Ambassador Cheng Speaks on Sino-German Relations

(Berlin) The new building of the Chinese Academy of the University of Frankfurt and the affiliated museum have now been completed. Chinese Ambassador Dr. Cheng Tianfang recently presided over the opening ceremony and delivered a speech, stating that since China and Germany signed a treaty of reconciliation on May 20, 1921, based on the principle of equality of rights, the friendship between the two sides has been unbroken and is a model of international relations. China is a raw material producing country, while Germany is a major industrial country, which can complement each other. This is why the trade between the two sides has developed endlessly. At this time, China's domestic transportation industry has been improved, and its natural resources have also been developed more, which can help the rapid development of trade between the two sides. At this point, Ambassador Cheng also elaborated on the philosophical concepts of China for more than 2,000 years, saying that they have many similarities with the modern philosophy of certain Western countries. China and Germany should cooperate in culture. It is a pity that certain European countries still have misunderstandings about the situation in China. The Chinese Academy of the University of Frankfurt will be able to dispel them. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

Authority on International Issues: Death of US Professor Moon

(New York) American authority on international issues, Dr. Moon Park, died today at the age of only 44. The doctor was born in New York City on June 5, 1892. He served as a history lecturer at Columbia University, and later rose to assistant professor of international relations. From 1918 to 1919, he served as a staff member of the American delegation to the Paris Peace Conference. He wrote many books on politics and international issues during his life. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

Full Text of the Draft Soviet Constitution (Part 1)

(Moscow) The Presidium of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union passed the following resolution: "The Presidium of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union, based on the report of Stalin, Chairman of the Constitutional Commission, hereby makes the following resolutions: Approve the draft Constitution of the Soviet Union proposed by the Constitutional Commission of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union; convene the All-Union Congress of Soviets to study the draft Constitution of the Soviet Union; stipulate that the All-Union Congress of Soviets will open on November 25, 1936; publish the draft Constitution of the Soviet Union for national discussion."

The original text of the draft Soviet Constitution is as follows:

Chapter 1: Social Organization

Article 1: The Union of Soviet Socialist Republics is a socialist state of workers and peasants.

Article 2: The political foundation of the Soviet Union is composed of Soviets of Workers' Deputies. These Soviets have grown and become stronger due to the overthrow of the landlord and bourgeois regime and the establishment of the proletarian dictatorship.

Article 3: All power in the Soviet Union belongs to the workers in urban and rural areas, in the form of Soviets of Workers' Deputies.

Article 4: The economic foundation of the Soviet Union is the socialist economic system and the socialist public ownership of the means and instruments of production. This is solidified and established by eliminating the capitalist economic system and abolishing the private ownership of the means and instruments of production, and abolishing the exploitation of man by man.

Article 5: Socialist public ownership in the Soviet Union is either in the form of state ownership (property owned by all the people) or in the form of cooperatives and collective farms (property owned by each collective farm and each cooperative association).

Article 6: Land and its mineral resources, water conservancy, forests, factories, mines, railways, water and air transportation, banks, transportation equipment, large state-run agricultural organizations (state-run farms, machine tractor stations, etc.), and the main part of urban housing, and industrial centers are all state property, that is, property owned by all the people.

Article 7: The public enterprises of collective farms and cooperative organizations, and their reproductive property, tools, collective farms, and the items cultivated and manufactured by cooperative associations, and all public buildings owned by them, are the public socialist property of collective farms and cooperative organizations. Each collective farm household may freely dispose of a piece of land attached to the farm, and auxiliary buildings on the farm's attached land, as well as houses, productive livestock, poultry, small agricultural tools, as stipulated in the agricultural labor union (collective farm) regulations, as private property.

Article 8: All land owned by collective farms can be used for an unlimited period of time, that is, permanently occupied.

Article 9: The socialist economic system is the dominant mode of the Soviet Union's economy. At the same time, the law permits small-scale private economies of farmers and family laborers, but only to the extent that they are based on personal labor and do not exploit the labor of others.

Article 10: The people's ownership of their labor income, savings, housing, and auxiliary family buildings, family economy, and objects for family use, as well as items for personal use and enjoyment, is protected by law.

Article 11: The economic life of the Soviet Union is directed and guided in accordance with the provisions of the national economic plan established by the state, in order to increase public wealth and continue to improve the material and cultural standards of workers, and to consolidate the independence and national defense of the Soviet Union.

Article 12: In the Soviet Union, according to the principle of "he who does not work, neither shall he eat," labor is the obligation of every able-bodied person. The Soviet Union is only realizing the socialist principle of "from each according to his ability, to each according to his work."

Chapter 2: State Organization

Article 13: The Union of Soviet Socialist Republics is a federal state composed of various Soviet socialist republics that have voluntarily joined together on the basis of equal rights, including the Russian Soviet Federated Socialist Republic, the Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic, the Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic, the Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic, the Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic, the Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic, the Turkmen Soviet Socialist Republic, the Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic, the Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic, the Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic, and the Kyrgyz Soviet Socialist Republic.

Article 14: The powers of the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics are represented by its highest organs of state power and state administrative organs. Its powers are as follows:

(A) Representing the Federation in international relations, concluding and ratifying foreign treaties;

(B) Declaring war and making peace;

(C) Permitting new republics to join the Soviet Union;

(D) Supervising the Soviet Constitution and ensuring that the constitutions of the federal republics do not conflict with the Soviet Constitution;

(E) Permitting modifications to the boundaries between republics;

(F) Organizing the defense of the Soviet Union and commanding the various armed forces of the Soviet Union;

(G) Guiding foreign trade based on state monopoly;

(H) Ensuring national security;

(I) Formulating the Soviet Union's national economic plan;

(J) Approving the Soviet Union's national budget, as well as the taxes and budgetary revenues of the Federation, the federal republics, and local areas;

(K) Managing the organization of banks, industry, and agriculture, and enterprises, as well as commercial enterprises with national significance;

(L) Managing transportation and transportation equipment;

(M) Managing the currency and credit system;

(N) Organizing state property insurance;

(O) Concluding and approving loans;

(P) Formulating the basic principles of land use, as well as the exploitation of mineral resources, forests, and water conservancy;

(Q) Formulating the basic principles of education and public health protection;

(R) Organizing a unified system of national economic auditing;

(S) Formulating basic labor laws;

(T) Formulating trial and legal procedures, penal law, and civil law;

(U) Formulating Soviet citizenship laws and foreign-related benefit laws;

(V) Issuing nationwide amnesty laws;

Article 15: The powers of the federal republics are limited only by the provisions of Article 14 of the Soviet Constitution. Except for these limitations, the federal republics may exercise their independent state powers. The Soviet Union guarantees the sovereignty of the federal republics.

Article 16: The federal republics each formulate their own constitutions, stipulating the specific form of the republic, and must not conflict with the Soviet Constitution.

Article 17: The federal republics reserve the right to freely withdraw from the Soviet Union.

Article 18: The territory of the federal republics may not be changed without their consent.

Article 19: Soviet laws have equal effect within the territory of all federal republics.

Article 20: If a federal republic's law conflicts with a federal law, the federal law must be implemented.

Article 21: Soviet citizens have only one citizenship qualification. Any citizen of a federal republic is a citizen of the Soviet Union.

Article 22: The Russian Federated Socialist Republic includes:

(A) The following regions: Azov-Black Sea, Far East, Western Siberia, Krasnoyarsk, North Caucasus;

(B) The following provinces: Voronezh, Eastern Siberia, Gorky, Western, Ivanovo, Kalinin, Kirov, Kuibyshev, Kursk, Leningrad, Moscow, Omsk, Orenburg, Saratov, Sverdlovsk, Northern, Stalingrad, Tambov, Chelyabinsk, Yaroslavl;

(C) The following autonomous Soviet socialist republics: Tatar, Bashkir, Dagestan, Buryat-Mongolia, Kabardino-Balkar, Kalmyk, Karelia, Komi, Crimea, Mari, Mordovian, German Volga, North Ossetian, Udmurt, Chechen-Ingush, Chuvash, Yakut;

(D) The following autonomous provinces: Adygea, Jewish, Karachay-Cherkess, Oirot, Khakass, Circassian;

Article 23: The Ukrainian Soviet Socialist Republic includes the following: Vinnytsia, Dnipropetrovsk, Donetsk, Kyiv, Odesa, Kharkiv, Chernihov, and the Moldavian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic.

Article 24: The Azerbaijani Soviet Socialist Republic includes the Nakhichevan Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic and the Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Republic.

Article 25: The Georgian Soviet Socialist Republic includes the Abkhazian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic, the Adjarian Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic, and the South Ossetian Autonomous Province.

Article 26: The Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic includes the Karakalpak Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic.

Article 27: The Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic includes the Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Province

Article 28.The Kazak Soviet Socialist Republic includes the following provinces: Aktyubinsk, Almaty, East Kazakhstan, West Kazakhstan, Karaganda, South Kazakhstan.

Article 29: The Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic, the Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic, the Turkmen Soviet Socialist Republic, and the Kyrgyz Soviet Socialist Republic do not include autonomous republics, regions, or provinces.

Article 30: The highest organ of state power in the Soviet Union is the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union (Verkhovny Soviet).

Chapter 3: The Highest Organ of State Power in the Soviet Union

Article 31: The Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union exercises the various powers of the Union of Soviet Socialist Republics stipulated in Article 14 of the Constitution, but does not, by virtue of the Constitution, participate in the functions of the various organs of the Soviet Union responsible to the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union. These organs are the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union, the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union, and the various People's Commissars of the Soviet Union.

Article 32: The legislative power of the Soviet Union is entirely exercised by the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union.

Article 33: The Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union includes two chambers, namely the Union Council and the Council of Nationalities.

Article 34: The Union Council is elected by the citizens of the Soviet Union, with one representative elected for every 300,000 people.

Article 35: Representatives to the Council of Nationalities are appointed by the Supreme Soviets of the federal republics and autonomous republics, and by the councils of workers' deputies of the autonomous provinces. Each federal republic elects ten representatives, each autonomous republic elects five representatives, and each autonomous province elects two representatives.

Article 36: The term of office of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union is four years.

Article 37: The two chambers of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union, namely the Union Council and the Council of Nationalities, enjoy equal powers.

Article 38: Both the Union Council and the Council of Nationalities may initiate legislation.

Article 39: Any law is established if it is passed by a majority of both chambers of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union.

Article 40: Laws passed by the Supreme Court of the Soviet Union are signed and promulgated by the Chairman and Secretary of the Presidium of the Supreme Court of the Soviet Union.

Article 41: The sessions of the Union Council and the Council of Nationalities must begin and end at the same time.

Article 42: The Union Council elects one Chairman of the Union Council and two Vice-Chairmen.

Article 43: The Council of Nationalities elects one Chairman of the Council of Nationalities and two Vice-Chairmen.

Article 44: The Chairmen of the Union Council and the Council of Nationalities preside over the meetings of their respective chambers and are responsible for handling internal affairs.

Article 45: Joint meetings of the two chambers of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union are presided over in rotation by the Chairman of the Union Council and the Chairman of the Council of Nationalities.

Article 46: The meetings of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union are convened by the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union twice a year. Temporary meetings are determined by the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union, or convened by the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet upon the request of a federal republic.

Article 47: If the Union Council and the Council of Nationalities have conflicting opinions on an issue, the issue must be transferred to a conciliation commission composed of an equal number of representatives from both chambers for resolution. If the conciliation commission cannot resolve the issue, or if its resolution cannot be agreed upon by one of the chambers, the issue must be submitted to both chambers for discussion again. If the two chambers still cannot reach a unanimous resolution, the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union should dissolve the Supreme Soviet and hold a new election.

Article 48: The Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union holds joint meetings of the two chambers to elect the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union, including one Chairman, four Vice-Chairmen, one Secretary of the Presidium, and thirty-one members of the Presidium. All activities of the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union are responsible to the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union.

Article 49: The powers of the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union are as follows:

(A) Convening meetings of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union;

(B) Issuing instructions and interpreting existing laws;

(C) Dissolving the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union and declaring a new election in accordance with Article 47 of the Soviet Constitution;

(D) Conducting referendums upon its own suggestion or upon the request of a federal republic;

(E) Revoking illegal resolutions and orders of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union and the People's Commissars of the various republics;

(F) During the recess of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union, exercising the powers of the Union and appointing the various People's Commissars upon the request of the Chairman of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union. This must be submitted to the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union for ratification;

(G) Awarding Soviet medals;

(H) Exercising the power of amnesty;

(I) Appointing and removing the supreme commanders of the Soviet armed forces;

(J) Declaring war if the Soviet Union is subjected to military attack during the recess of the Supreme Soviet;

(K) Declaring general mobilization and partial mobilization;

(L) Ratifying international treaties;

(M) Appointing and dismissing plenipotentiary representatives of the Soviet Union abroad;

(N) Accepting the presentation of credentials from foreign diplomatic representatives.

Article 50: The Union Council and the Council of Nationalities each organize a credentials review committee to review the qualifications of the representatives of their respective chambers. Each chamber accepts the recommendations of the credentials review committee and decides whether to recognize or revoke the qualifications of the representatives.

Article 51: The Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union organizes committees for investigation and auditing of various issues when necessary. All organs and officials must accept the demands of these committees and provide the necessary materials and documents.

Article 52: The representatives of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union may not be accused or arrested without the consent of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union, or without the consent of the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union during the recess of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union.

Article 53: After the expiration of the term of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union, or after the Supreme Soviet is dissolved before the expiration of its term, the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union retains its powers until the new Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union organizes a new Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union.

Article 54: After the expiration of the term of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union, or after the Supreme Soviet is dissolved before the expiration of its term, the Presidium of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union must announce the re-election within two months after the expiration or dissolution of the Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union.

Article 55: The newly elected Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union must be convened by the Presidium of the outgoing Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union within one month after the election.

Article 56: The Supreme Soviet of the Soviet Union holds joint meetings of the two chambers to organize the Council of People's Commissars, the government of the Soviet Union. (The complete text of Chapter 3 will continue) (TASS dispatch, 12th)

The Palestine Issue: Arabs Attack British Police Officer 29

Jerusalem: A British police officer was attacked twice yesterday. In one incident, Deputy Superintendent Sigrid was seriously wounded. Sigrid, accompanied by a police officer, was patrolling in a car when, while driving between the St. Stephen's Gate and the Herod's Gate, they were shot at by two people hiding in a dark corner. Sigrid was hit by a bullet, seriously wounding his chest and shoulder. The police officer in the car immediately returned fire, felling one of the assailants. He died shortly after in the hospital. Police dogs are currently tracking down the other assailant. The residence of Farah Tye, Deputy Superintendent of Police in Nazareth, was also shot at during the night. It is widely believed that Sigrid was attacked because Arabs were jealous of his dedication to duty. Last night, a passenger train was bombed while traveling to Kalkilya, seriously injuring four Jews and slightly injuring twelve Jews and one Arab. (Reuters, 13th)

(London) Chancellor Chamberlain's speech on June 10, advocating the lifting of sanctions against Italy, has caused great shock in diplomatic and political circles. The French and Belgian ambassadors to London both visited the Foreign Office today to discuss the impact of this speech. It is reported that although the Chancellor's so-called change of attitude by Britain has not yet been formally endorsed by the government, France and Belgium are both greatly surprised. The British government believes that since Argentina has recently suggested lifting sanctions against Italy, it would be unbefitting of Britain, as a major power, to hide behind South American countries. Therefore, Britain may take the lead in this matter. However, even if sanctions are to be lifted, this should not be taken as Britain's recognition of Italy's annexation of Abyssinia. He said: "At a time when the world is facing a crisis, it is regrettable that a powerful nation like England is governed by people who are indecisive." The National Government, through Foreign Secretary Eden, has declared to the world that it intends to uphold peace and must take risks. At the same time, it has advised the people to support collective security mechanisms and the rule of law. Now, Chancellor Chamberlain says that what was done before should be reversed. Why is this? "If the Chancellor's words do not represent the government, then is it not strange that the Chancellor, at a time of national crisis, expresses his views on foreign policy in a personal capacity?" (Havas, 12th)

(London) The Welsh branch of the League of Nations Union and other organizations have expressed opposition to Chancellor Chamberlain's speech. They have resolved to send telegrams to Prime Minister Baldwin, Foreign Secretary Eden, and Chancellor Chamberlain, saying, "The Chancellor's remarks are astounding, and this association is very dissatisfied." (Havas, 13th)

(London) According to general observation, Foreign Secretary Eden will likely make a statement to the House of Commons before the Extraordinary Meeting of the League of Nations Council, explaining that the Italian-Abyssinian war has now ended. Therefore, the current sanctions measures are of no benefit to continue implementing in the long run. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini will also issue a statement, reaffirming his guarantee that Italy is still willing to participate in the work of appeasing Europe and promising that all Italian facilities in Abyssinia will be based on generosity and freedom, and that the inherent rights of the natives will be recognized. Sanctions Are Not a Permanent Task, Emphasis on Anglo-German Understanding

(London) Chancellor Chamberlain's speech advocated the lifting of sanctions against Italy and mentioned a document distributed by Viscount Cecil to the members of the League of Nations, in which he urged the members to pressure the government to continue implementing sanctions, and even intensify them. The Chancellor criticized this policy, saying that it would cause future harm. Today, The Times published an editorial criticizing the Chancellor's speech, saying that it is a mistake for Britain to unilaterally exert pressure and allow Italian goods to enter, just as the opposite action of imposing sanctions six months ago was a mistake. The so-called "sanctions," which were mistakenly called, are not a permanent task. Since they were jointly implemented as a test, they can only be jointly terminated. This is something that everyone knows. After encountering an international failure in using the League of Nations Covenant to contain war, the general public is paying attention to the proper repair of peace institutions (both positive and negative), and how and when the powers concerned can decide to terminate their attempted passive economic resistance plan against aggression is secondary. The report also strongly stated that the exchange of views between Britain and Germany is of constructive value and is conducive to general peace in Europe. It is now urgent to clear the thorns in the way so that British Ambassador Sir Phipps can go to Berlin to engage in negotiations. (Reuters, 13th)

(Berlin) The British government raised questions with Germany at the beginning of last month, but the German government has not yet responded. The National Socialist Party has not indicated when the reply will be submitted, and their tone suggests that Führer Hitler is quite embarrassed by the British questions and is finding it difficult to submit a reply for the time being. Diplomatic circles believe that the government may wait until after the Extraordinary Meetings of the League of Nations Council and Assembly before responding. Moreover, the British questions are detailed, clear, and precise, so the German reply may use generalized language to avoid answering directly. Close associates of Führer Hitler recently declared that since the German government officially announced the abolition of the Locarno Treaty on March 7, it has repeatedly issued declarations and diplomatic documents expressing its desire for peace. However, the British questions still show suspicion and distrust, which is regrettable. (Havas, 13th)

Secret Document on Reform of the League of Nations by Spanish Representative 33

Using Article 11 of the Covenant as the Backbone, Each Country Can Reserve Its Position on Article 16

(Paris) Regarding the discussion on the reorganization of the League of Nations, "L'Agence Économique" recently reported that the Spanish representative to the League of Nations, Madariaga, yesterday distributed a "Confidential Note on the Amendment of the Implementation Methods of the League of Nations Covenant" to certain member states. The content stated that the original text of the Covenant should not be amended, but the implementation methods could be changed. On the one hand, it advocated that all member states should be able to adopt a reserved attitude when implementing the various sanction measures stipulated in Article 16 of the Covenant. On the other hand, it also proposed adding an annex, based on Article 11 of the Covenant, and inviting the United States, Japan, and Germany to sign and participate, so as to prevent war. According to Article 11 of the Covenant: "It is hereby declared that any war or threat of war, whether directly or indirectly affecting any Member of the League, is a matter of concern to the entire League, and the League shall take action to safeguard peace among nations. At the request of any Member of the League, the Secretary-General shall immediately convene a meeting of the Council. It is also declared that any circumstance affecting international relations which threatens to disturb international peace or good understanding between nations is the right of any Member of the League to bring to the attention of the Assembly or the Council in a friendly manner." (Havas, 13th)

French Chamber of Deputies Passes Forty-Hour Work Week System 34

Labor Strikes Largely Resolved

(Paris) Today, after a full day of debate, the Chamber of Deputies passed the government's forty-hour work week bill by a vote of 385 to 175. At the same time, the strike situation continued to ease. It is estimated that 200,000 workers have returned to work in the past 24 hours. Labor and management in the metallurgical factories signed a collective contract at the Ministry of the Interior tonight, which is the most important aspect of resolving the strikes. The dock workers in Le Havre threatened to strike, but this was canceled because the employers had agreed to increase wages by 12 percent. The situation in the north has improved significantly today. 35 factories in Lille and 38 factories in Roubaix have started work. Currently, only over 10,000 people in Valenciennes are still insisting on not returning to work. (Reuters, 12th)

(Paris) The Chamber of Deputies met this morning to discuss the 40-hour work week system bill. After eight hours of discussion, it was finally passed by a vote of 385 to 175. Thus, all five bills on social and labor issues proposed by Prime Minister Léon Blum have been passed by the Chamber of Deputies. At 5:00 PM, they were immediately submitted to the Senate. The Senate immediately convened at 5:15 PM and, after 15 minutes of discussion, decided to organize a special committee to review them, so that they could be submitted for discussion next Tuesday. Prime Minister Léon Blum delivered a speech in the Senate, referring to the labor strikes, saying that if there is any disruption to order, the current government will definitely stop it. The government will also take strict measures to punish anyone with suspicious intentions to interfere with the labor strikes. (Havas, 12th)

(Paris) Representatives of labor and management in the metallurgical industry held a meeting at the Ministry of Labor at 6:00 PM today and immediately signed an agreement, thus resolving the labor strikes in the industry. The striking workers are scheduled to return to work next Monday. This is the most important event of the day. The strikes in the wholesale and retail butcher shops in the capital were also declared over today, and they are scheduled to resume work tomorrow morning. The bakery union issued a statement saying that labor and management in the industry signed a work contract in 1929, stipulating wage ratios. In the past year, representatives of both sides have also organized a joint committee to jointly study methods of reforming the bakery industry. The relationship between the two sides is very harmonious, and the workers have never intended to strike. Currently, there are only 256,476 striking workers in the Seine region. Almost all construction workers have returned to work. The workers in the small woodworking and locksmith industries are scheduled to return to work tomorrow or next Monday. Several minor accidents occurred in the province today, and 41 workers were arrested, 39 of whom were released soon after. 736 factories in the Nord department have had their striking workers leave. The metallurgical factories in Maubeuge and the Sambre River basin are all scheduled to resume work tomorrow. The Ministry of Labor recently issued a long statement on the labor strike situation, commenting on the resumption of work throughout the country. Local authorities have also reported local situations to the Ministry of the Interior, and the tone is very optimistic. Therefore, the end of the labor strikes is not far away. (Havas, 12th)

All Industries Must Not Accept Stolen Goods as Collateral for Loans 57

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance recently received a secret report that private smugglers are mortgaging undeclared goods to banks in order to transport them for sale. The Ministry considers the receipt of stolen goods on which taxes have not been paid to be a violation of the criminal law on stolen goods. Banks and money shops that lend money on this type of collateral are essentially receiving stolen goods on which taxes have not been paid, which is a violation of the criminal law. It is imperative to issue strict warnings. On the 13th, a special telegram was sent to all banking and money shop guilds across the country, instructing all banks and shops that when undertaking goods as collateral, if the goods are imported goods, they should provide the stack receipt and bill of lading at the original port of import, and then obtain a certificate from the customs for the import tax receipt to be provided together. For those transported from the original port of import to various places, in addition to providing the stack receipt and bill of lading, a certificate should be obtained from the local chamber of commerce or the corresponding industry guild, proving that the goods have been issued a transportation permit by the customs and are allowed to be transported and sold after being registered by the guild. If the above certificate cannot be obtained and there is suspicion of tax evasion, the bill of lading and stack receipt should be detained and reported to the local authorities or directly submitted to the Ministry for verification. If the banks and shops knowingly accept stolen goods on which taxes have not been paid as collateral, once verified, the managers of the banks and shops will be severely punished according to the criminal law on stolen goods. (Central News Agency, 13th)

The Sino-British Boundary Demarcation Issue in Yunnan and Burma 67

— Ji Nan

As early as 1763, Britain concluded the "Seven Years' War" and took India as its territory. In 1886 (the twelfth year of the reign of Emperor Guangxu of the Qing Dynasty), it further seized Burma, breaching our defense barrier, thus opening the southwest gateway of our country. Therefore, the demarcation of the Yunnan-Burma boundary became a matter of utmost urgency.

According to records, during the reigns of Emperor Qianlong and Jiaqing of the Qing Dynasty, the Jinsha River was regarded as the natural boundary line between Yunnan and Burma. When Britain annexed Burma, Zeng Jize, our minister to Britain, still strongly advocated using the Jinsha River as the boundary during negotiations with the British Foreign Secretary Lord Clarendon. However, no boundary treaty was concluded at that time; only memoranda were exchanged and kept on file. It was not until 1894 (the twentieth year of the reign of Emperor Guangxu) that Xue Fucheng, our minister to Britain, negotiated with the British Foreign Secretary Lord Rosebery on the boundary demarcation, and the Supplementary Convention between Great Britain and China relating to Burma and Tibet was concluded. This convention divided the Yunnan-Burma boundary into two sections, north and south, with the peak of Mount Hkakabo Razi at 25 degrees 35 minutes north latitude and 98 degrees 14 minutes east longitude as the center. The southern section was further divided into three segments, starting from Mount Hkakabo Razi, southwest to the Taiping River as the first segment; from the confluence of the Taiping River and the Khunlong River (i.e., the Galong River), southwest to the Shweli River as the second segment; and from the confluence of the Shweli River and the Mengmao River, southeast to the Meijiang River as the third segment. A map of the Yunnan-Burma boundary was signed as an annex. The northern section (north of 25 degrees 35 minutes north latitude) was left as an outstanding issue due to disputes over the Triangle Area (aka the "Wild Man's Mountain"). In 1896 (the twenty-second year of the reign of Emperor Guangxu), China and France concluded the Yunnan-Vietnam Treaty, ceding Mengdao (Menglian) to France. Britain believed that the two places were within the Jianghong boundary and violated Article 5 of the Supplementary Convention between Great Britain and China relating to Burma and Tibet, which stated that "China shall not cede the whole or part of Menglian and Jianghong to other countries without prior agreement between China and Britain," and demanded a new treaty. Thus, the 1897 (the twenty-third year of the reign of Emperor Guangxu) Burma Convention with Nineteen Additional Articles was concluded, which was roughly the same as the original convention, but the boundary line was pushed further east, resulting in even greater losses for our country. In 1899 (the twenty-fifth year of the reign of Emperor Guangxu), China and Britain jointly appointed officials to survey the southern section of the boundary. Unexpectedly, complications arose again, and the section from the confluence of the Nampa and Namtin rivers to the point where the Namma River flows into the Nanka River could not be surveyed. At that time, our representatives Liu Wansheng and Chen Can, based on the Xue's map attached to the treaty, assigned all areas belonging to Ban Hong (Upper Hulu) to Yunnan and all areas belonging to Ban Kuang (Lower Hulu) to Burma, following the Menglin Mountain, Pachang Mountain, Gongming Mountain, to the Nanka River, using the mountain ridges and rivers as the boundary, and assigned the Mengjiao, Mengdong, and Menglian Tusi to Yunnan. However, the British side suddenly raised objections, pointing to Kongming Mountain near Lancang County as Gongming Mountain, attempting to assign the Mengga, Gongnong, Gongyong, Xiaomengnong areas belonging to Mengjiao and the Mengbo and Ximeng areas belonging to Menglian to Burma, which was obviously inconsistent with the text of the treaty. After repeated concessions and compromises between the two sides, the total boundary line involved in the negotiations was divided into five colors: yellow, blue, purple, green, and red, which is known as the Five-Color Line of the southern section. They are briefly described as follows:

The yellow line is the initial line determined by Liu Wansheng and Chen Can according to Xue's map. It starts from the confluence of the Nampa and Namtin rivers, follows the high mountains, passes Menglin Mountain, follows the mountain ridge, passes Pachang Mountain, crosses the Dananggung River, ascends Guangkan Mountain, reaches Gongming Mountain, follows the mountain ridge to the east, crosses the Namma River, passes Shantong Yancheng, and reaches the Nanka River, follows the river to the confluence of the Nanshui River. All areas east of Menglin Mountain belonging to Ban Hong, Yongbang villages east of Pachang Mountain, Gongnong, Gongyong, Mengmao under the jurisdiction of Mengjiao, wild villages east of Gongming Mountain, wild Ka of Shantong Yancheng west of the Nanka River, and areas under the jurisdiction of Zhenbian and Menglian Tusi are assigned to Yunnan. All areas west of Menglin Mountain belonging to Ban Nong, villages of Bankuang west of Pachang Mountain, and wild Ka west of Gongming Mountain and Nanka River, such as Eleven Families of Zhaohua, Nuokan Wu, and Lower Mang Leng, are assigned to Burma.

The blue line is the concession line proposed by Liu Wansheng and Chen Can. After ascending Guangkan Mountain according to the yellow line, it deviates east to Nanlan Mountain, then slightly east and north to Antun Mountain, then slightly east and south to Nanwa Mountain, southeast to the Bantingshan behind Black River, turns west, follows the watershed between the Namma and Nanxiang rivers to Nongqiu Mountain, goes down along the slope to the source of the Nanka River, and follows the river to the confluence of the Nanyong River. The Xin'a and Mengga villages under the jurisdiction of Ban Hong and Mengjiao, the Xiling and Banting villages under the jurisdiction of Zhenbian and Lizhang, Ku Xing, Nanxiang, Nongqiu Mountain, Ximeng Mountain, and Guantian, Yongguang, Mannong, Lengkan, Bangbei, Yonghei, and Suxing villages on the east bank of the Nanka River all belong to Yunnan. Shaoxing, Shaoba, Upper and Lower Kunma, Shantong, Yancheng, Eleven Families of Zhaohua, and all Ka lands belong to Burma.

The purple line is the line shown by the ministry. After ascending Guangkan Mountain according to the blue line, it turns east to Nuoguo Mountain, south to Nanlan Mountain, deviates east to Antun Mountain, goes around to Nanwa Mountain, follows the mountain ridge, southeast to Bantingshan behind Black River, turns west to the head of the Kuxing River, follows the river to the confluence of the Nanxiang River, and then follows down to the Nanka River, where it still merges with the blue line. This means that the north and south ends completely coincide with the blue line, while the middle section advances eastward. Although Naka, Longmei, Jianmeng, Mengsuo belonging to Maoshou, Boxiang, and Heila east of the Kuxing River, and Talang and Nanbing villages south of the Nanxiang River are still within the Yunnan border, Zuoke, Banqian, and Nianhe west of the Kuxing River, and Yongting, Guojiao, Wan Mine, Banga, and Banshi villages of Ximeng Mountain all belong to Burma.

The green line is the line reduced by the British official Scott. Its northern section is completely the same as this color line, but when it reaches the confluence of the Kuxing River and the Nanxiang River, it goes south along the mountain ridge, passes Banshun, Fuyan, Bangbei, and Kuhei to the Nanka River, and then merges with the blue line (i.e., the purple line). In this case, Talang, Nanbing, Guantian, Fulang, Tongban, Yongguang, Mannong, Lengkan, Bangbei, and other villages all belong to the Burmese border.

The red line is the line drawn by the British official Scott himself. It starts from the confluence of the Nampa and Namtin rivers, follows the mountain ridge, to the north of Menglin Mountain, deviates east through Nanban, Ban Hong, Xin'a and other places, goes south along the mountain ridge to Nuoguo Mountain, turns south and east to Nanwa Mountain, then northeast, passes Manling, and then follows the Nandai Mountain through Black River Head to Banting, and then follows the watershed between the Kuxing River and the Meilu River southward, to the west of Zhenbianshubang, then southwest along the watershed between the Meilu River, and merges with the green line. In this way, Ban Hong, Xin'a, Mengga, Gongnong, Xiaomengnong, Manling and other places in the north, and Naka, Yuemei, Fameng, Heila, Maoshou, Mengsuo, Boxiang and other places in the middle are all assigned to the Burmese border.

In the above-mentioned boundary demarcation situation, the northern section (north of Mount Hkakabo Razi) has become an outstanding issue, and the southern section (south of Mount Hkakabo Razi) has not been determined due to different opinions on the boundary line. Moreover, the British side used the excuse that the map used by our side was not the original map signed by the two ministers Xue and Rosebery, and insisted on using the red line to determine the boundary, so the negotiations failed to produce results, and the Sino-British-French demarcation of the Yunnan-Burma boundary was suspended, and has not been resolved for forty years. Since the founding of the Republic of China, the country has been plagued by many problems, and the border issues have not been given attention. The imperceptible encroachment by the British, such as secretly shifting boundary markers and cultivating land across the border, has been heard from time to time. Since they arbitrarily invade, they do not value the boundary, so there is no need to urgently determine it. However, their ambition to encroach eastward has never been slightly restrained due to the undetermined boundary. Moreover, the Triangle Area in the northern section is close to the source of the Yangtze River, which is a shortcut to open up the Yangtze River; the Ban Hong in the southern section has extremely many minerals and is a place rich in resources, which the British have coveted day and night. The Pianma Incident and the Jiangxinpo Incident in the twenty-third year were manifestations of their ambition to use the undetermined boundary in the northern section to extend their power to Sichuan and Kangding, and to attempt to directly descend into the Yangtze River basin. The Banfan Incident of the same year was an activity within the undetermined boundary in the southern section, with the aim of seizing mining rights.

Since our southwestern border has been repeatedly nibbled away, the government has reiterated its previous proposal and proposed to send officials to survey the boundary. Thus, the Sino-British Joint Committee for the Survey of the Yunnan-Burma Boundary was established in April of the twenty-fourth year, composed of two members each from China and Britain, and one neutral member selected by the chairman of the Council of the League of Nations. Since the establishment of the committee, a year has passed. The survey work has not been long before it was temporarily suspended due to the severe miasma on the Yunnan border, which made it impossible to survey. Unfortunately, at this time of prolonged indecision, on February 21 of this year, more than 200 British soldiers suddenly entered the Yunnan border, occupied the Jingmao area belonging to Lancang County, and set up various military projects. Their intention was to create a "fait accompli" as an excuse to encroach during the boundary survey. However, the results of the thorough investigation by the boundary survey committee stated that it was actually a misunderstanding by the British survey team, and the committee members returning to Beijing also stated in their talks that the boundary survey process was quite smooth. However, although we dare not be certain what serious significance the British intrusion into Jingmao has, it can be asserted that there are still many thorns in the future of the boundary affairs.

Considering the five-color boundary lines in the disputed southern section, even according to the yellow line, the concessions have been much greater than the memorandum made by Minister Zeng, who advocated using the Jinsha River as the natural boundary after Britain's conquest of Burma in 1886. Moreover, based on the Supplementary Convention between Great Britain and China relating to Burma and Tibet of 1894 and the Burma Convention with Nineteen Additional Articles of 1897, there is no reason to make further concessions. We observe that the numerous complications in the repeated boundary surveys and the long-term indecision clearly indicate where the responsibility lies. Therefore, whether the Sino-British-French Yunnan-Burma boundary demarcation can proceed smoothly in the future depends on whether the British have sincerity and whether they can base it on a fair spirit and determine a reasonable boundary line based on history and geography.

Statistics on Smuggled Goods Arriving in Jinan in April and May 70

The total value of the goods is approximately 600,000 yuan. Customs losses exceed one million yuan. Jinan's commerce is greatly affected.

Jinan Correspondence: A large number of smuggled goods from a certain country have arrived in Jinan. Taking the goods arriving in Jinan from Tianjin from June 1st to 11th as an example, there are approximately 300 to 400 pieces of cigarette paper, more than 320 pieces of rayon, and more than 120 tons and 9 bags of white sugar, with a total value of approximately 230,000 yuan. Customs losses are also estimated at 50,000 to 60,000 yuan. As for the quantity of smuggled goods in April and May, according to the statistics of the freight documents of the Jinpu and Jiaoji Railways, a large number of rayon, cigarette paper, and white sugar arrived in Jinan. The number of rayon transported along the Jiaoji Railway to Zhoucun is particularly alarming. Jinan's commerce has been greatly affected, and the domestic silk market has been particularly hit. The customs losses are estimated at more than one million yuan. The daily quantity of smuggled goods arriving in Jinan and Zhoucun and the customs losses are detailed below.

Quantity in April

(A) Rayon: Arrived in Jinan on April 5th, 231 pieces; 122 pieces on the 6th; 52 pieces on the 11th; 54 pieces on the 12th; 116 pieces on the 13th; 91 pieces on the 14th; 255 pieces on the 15th; 183 pieces on the 16th; 224 pieces on the 17th; 120 pieces on the 19th; 4 pieces on the 20th, and another 127 pieces; 25 pieces on the 21st; 227 pieces on the 22nd; 52 pieces on the 23rd, totaling 1,853 pieces. (B) Cigarette Paper: Arrived in Jinan from Tianjin on April 16th, 102 pieces; 136 pieces on the 17th; 7 pieces on the 20th; 50 pieces on the 22nd; 10 pieces on the 23rd, totaling 305 pieces. (C) Rayon transported from Jinan along the Jiaoji Railway to Zhoucun: 82 pieces on April 5th; 317 pieces on the 6th; 338 pieces on the 7th; 139 pieces on the 9th; 102 pieces on the 10th; 132 pieces on the 11th; 74 pieces on the 12th; 438 pieces on the 13th; 527 pieces on the 14th; 387 pieces on the 15th; 735 pieces on the 16th; 411 pieces on the 17th; 445 pieces on the 19th; 120 pieces on the 20th, and another 806 pieces; 243 pieces on the 21st, totaling 5,296 pieces. In total, there were 7,454 pieces of smuggled rayon and cigarette paper on the Jinpu and Jiaoji Railways.

Quantity in May

(A) May 5th, 5 pieces arrived in Jinan from Tianjin; 36 pieces on the 7th; 33 pieces on the 8th; 40 pieces on the 10th; 52 pieces on the 13th; 46 pieces on the 14th; 18 pieces on the 16th; 243 pieces on the 20th; 8 pieces on the 21st; 250 pieces on the 22nd; 10 pieces on the 24th; 40 pieces on the 25th; 70 pieces on the 26th; 10 pieces on the 27th; 30 pieces on the 28th; 3 pieces on the 29th, totaling 794 pieces. (B) Cigarette Paper: 133 pieces arrived in Jinan from Tianjin on May 1st; 15 pieces on the 2nd; 22 pieces on the 3rd; 32 pieces on the 4th; 36 pieces on the 5th; 7 pieces on the 6th; 17 pieces on the 8th; 66 pieces on the 10th; 66 pieces on the 11th; 53 pieces on the 13th; 84 pieces on the 14th; 139 pieces on the 15th; 12 pieces on the 16th; 82 pieces on the 17th; 16 pieces on the 18th; 34 pieces on the 20th; 50 pieces on the 22nd; 107 pieces on the 23rd; 91 pieces on the 24th; 45 pieces on the 26th, totaling 1,109 pieces. In addition, from May 1st to 31st, there were 4,420 tons of white sugar transported from Tianjin to Jinan.

Customs Losses

The total of smuggled rayon from Tianjin and Jiaoji Railways in April and May is 17,536 pieces. The average weight of each piece is approximately 6 kilograms, totaling 105,216 kilograms. The value of each piece is approximately 170 yuan, with a total value of 2,981,112 yuan. There are 1,414 pieces of cigarette paper, with each piece weighing approximately 160 kilograms, totaling 226,240 kilograms. The value of each piece is 160 yuan, estimated at a total value of 226,240 yuan. The total value of the above two items is 524,352 yuan. The customs and all additional taxes are approximately one times the total value, so the customs losses in the past two months should be more than one million yuan. The over 4,000 tons of untaxed white sugar are not included. The numbers in this one area are already so large, and if other areas are included, the numbers would be even more shocking. (11th)

Construction of the Guang-Shan Railway 71

The Ministry of Railways has agreed to allocate construction funds, but whether it will be state-run or province-run is yet to be decided.

Guangzhou Communication: Transportation between Guangzhou and Shantou has long relied on maritime routes. Since the completion of the provincial highway main lines, transportation between Guangzhou and Shantou can be done by automobile. However, the provincial government considers Shantou an important commercial port in the Dongjiang region, and products from various counties in the Dongjiang region can be exported through Shantou. Therefore, there is an urgent need to build the Guang-Shan Railway to connect with the Yue-Han Railway, so as to gradually implement the Premier's southwest railway network plan. Therefore, the provincial government instructed the Yue-Han Railway South Section Bureau last year to send technicians to survey the Guang-Shan railway line. The survey has been completed. Later, due to the lack of construction funds, it was initially planned to be jointly supervised by the government and merchants, but it did not materialize due to various reasons. When Minister of Railways Zhang Jia'ao came to the south, Provincial Chairman Lin Yunkai brought up the issue of building the Guang-Shan Railway for discussion and requested that the Ministry of Railways allocate funds for construction. The Ministry of Railways then proposed that the construction of the Guang-Shan Railway would require tens of millions of dollars, which would be allocated from the construction public debt funds or borrowed from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee as construction funds. According to news from the provincial government yesterday, the provincial government has decided to actively prepare for the construction of the Guang-Shan Railway in order to connect transportation in various counties in the Dongjiang region. At the same time, the provincial government has received a reply from the Ministry of Railways stating that the construction funds for the Guang-Shan Railway have been approved. The Ministry of Railways will send personnel to the south to discuss the construction plan with the provincial government. After the Ministry of Railways' technical director arrives in the south, preparations will begin. As for the future management of the Guang-Shan Railway, whether it will be state-run or province-run, it is still to be decided through consultation. Recently, Provincial Chairman Lin sent a telegram to Li Xiangen, director of the Yue-Han Railway South Section Bureau, to consult with Minister Zhang in Beijing as soon as possible regarding the Guang-Shan Railway's progress.

General Situation of Land Use in Beijing 72

The total area is approximately 69,871 mu. In the future, land in Beijing will become more uniform and orderly.

Nanjing Communication: The Nanjing Municipal Government has been very active in organizing land administration in recent years, and the results are excellent. The following is a record of the general situation of land use:

Determining the Political District

The Central Political District is the construction area for central government offices. The Capital Construction Committee designed and formulated drawings to delineate the land along the north and south sides of Zhongshan Road within Zhongshan Gate in the old imperial city area, with an area of more than 4,000 mu. Later, due to the increase in the population of Beijing and the increasing lack of housing, the Beijing Municipal Government delineated a portion of the south side, about 2,500 mu, as a residential area, which was contracted by the people for construction. The land price was set at six yuan per square meter, and an additional construction fee of twenty yuan per square meter was charged. Now the entire plan has been finalized, and it can be carried out according to the plan after the collection procedures are completed.

Newly Developed Residential Area

Since the establishment of the capital in Beijing, the population has increased dramatically. The original housing supply cannot meet the demand, and most of it is located in the south of the city, stretching for more than ten miles from Xiaguan to Gulou. Government offices are lined up, and housing is scarce, resulting in rising house prices and rents. The citizens feel extremely distressed about the housing problem. The Beijing Municipal Government, in view of this, planned in June of the 19th year to collect more than 2,000 mu of land in the Dafang Lane, Lao Caishi, and Gulin Temple areas in the north of the city to develop a new residential area, which is divided into four districts. The first district has an area of 417.0615 mu. After deducting 27.7479 mu for public land, all the residential land of 389.8536 mu is divided into 290 lots. The land price is set at eight yuan per square meter, and an additional construction fee of twenty yuan is charged. It was completely released in the 23rd year. Public construction and housing projects in the district have now been largely completed. The second and third districts have not been organized because the location is relatively remote. The fourth district has an area of 418.0216 mu. After deducting 20.6551 mu for public land, all the residential land of 397.3665 mu is divided into 295 lots. It was completely released in the 24th year. Various construction projects in the district have now begun. In addition to developing new residential areas, the Beijing Municipal Government also plans to develop low-cost housing areas for the convenience of citizens. First, three places in the city, including Wudingmen, Gonghoushan, and Hepingmen, were acquired, with a total area of more than 34 mu, and low-cost housing was built for citizens to rent. It was completed in the 24th year and began to be rented out. Now, land is still being acquired in six places, including Mofan Road, Hongmiao, Guangdong Villa, Mint Factory, Laohutou, and Xinghuacun, with a total area of more than 440 mu. They are all being developed as low-cost housing areas and have now been completely acquired.

Land Re-planning

The abandoned land on both sides of the newly built roads in Beijing and the remaining land acquired due to road construction, which do not meet the prescribed construction standards, are all re-planned by the Beijing Municipal Government and reorganized before the people can contract for construction. The Zhongshan East Road, Daxing Palace, Taiping Road, and Menlian Bridge sections have been reorganized in accordance with this re-planning plan. The following is a classified comparison table of the land acquisition area in Nanjing:

In addition to the area listed in the table on the right, there are also rural areas and Pukou, etc., with a total urban area of 69,871 mu (city system).

Fire Arson Plot Suspected Case in Fuzhou 73

Insurance premium of more than 240,000 yuan. Fang Meizhen was detained pending trial.

Fuzhou Communication: A sensational suspected arson plot case has recently occurred in Minyuan, Fuzhou. The Chadao area of ​​Cangxiazhou in Nantai is a place where ships from the upper reaches of the Minjiang River gather. There is an Anping warehouse on the riverbank, which is specially rented to people for storing tea, fragrant mushrooms, dried bamboo shoots, and groceries transported from various counties in northern Fujian. The warehouse owner is Fang Meizhen, who subleased it from Southeast Bank. At 2:30 in the morning on June 1, a fire alarm suddenly occurred. All the fire brigades in the city rushed to rescue. By 3:00, the fire was extinguished. The warehouse owner, Fang Meizhen, went to the Minhou Local Procuratorate at about 10:00 am that morning to file a case. After a brief interrogation, he was released on bail. Afterwards, it was found that the warehouse's cargo owners held a huge amount of cargo fire insurance totaling 241,000 yuan, including 65,000 yuan from Siming Company, 20,000 yuan from Taishan Company, 21,000 yuan from Yongfeng Company, 16,000 yuan from Chanson Foreign Company, 24,000 yuan from Taikoo Company, 10,000 yuan from Sun Company, 39,000 yuan from Seaborne Company, 6,000 yuan from Yuchang Company, 10,000 yuan from China Company for building insurance, 23,000 yuan from Yangtze River Company, and 7,000 yuan from Baozhong Company. The amount of loss broke the record of fire insurance compensation in Fuzhou. Each company suspected that its behavior was suspicious, so it telegraphed Shanghai Yizhong, Sanyi, Lu Yishi Moore, and San Justice Line, Ge Jichen, Li Situn, Yin Maozhi, and Laude to come to Fujian by plane on the 2nd for inspection. The Minhou Local Procuratorate also went to the scene for inspection on the 5th by Prosecutor Deng Yinan. According to the warehouse owner, Fang Meizhen, in the case filing, the cause of the fire was caused by the neighboring Longcheng Tea House setting off firecrackers for a funeral. Prosecutor Deng, in order to conduct a careful investigation, opened a temporary investigation court in Longcheng Tea House and summoned He, a cohabitant, who stated that the deceased was not yet 30 years old on the day of the funeral. According to Fujian customs, firecrackers could not be set off, so no firecrackers were set off when the coffin was carried out. However, when returning to Yuyu, a string of Bai Zi cannons worth thirteen copper coins was set off by the river in Chadao to invite auspiciousness. After investigating, there were more than ten houses and two or three high walls between the river in Chadao and the warehouse. After the interrogation, the prosecutor personally went to the river for inspection and drew a picture for record. The next day, Prosecutor Deng also summoned Lu Yishi Moore and Sanyi to inquire about the results of the inspection for reference. The warehouse owner, Fang Meizhen, was allowed to be released on bail for 3,000 yuan. Currently, due to lack of bail, he is still in custody. According to people in the insurance industry, all the Chinese and foreign head offices are paying close attention to the fire insurance claim of this warehouse. They will file charges against all parties involved in accordance with the law to find out the truth and curb the evil trend of fire insurance claims. (June 10)

Changshu 77

Cocoon firms suppress cocoon prices

The sericulturists in Lanqiao and other places here have all harvested their cocoons and are waiting for a good price to sell. Unexpectedly, recently, Shaochang Cocoon Firm in the area deliberately suppressed the cocoon price, which is less than 30 yuan per dan, which is too different from the current Wuxi market price. Moreover, the co-breeding cocoon households improved by the guidance station are no different from ordinary cocoons. As a result, many cocoon households are watching and unwilling to sell. Now the cocoon firm is asking the township head to find a way to reward the co-breeding households with 600 yuan, which will be distributed by the township head. As for the cocoon price, it is still the same as ordinary cocoons. Currently, the breeding households add six yuan per dan for the co-breeding households of previous years and disagree with the method proposed by the cocoon firm. They have telegraphed the director of the guidance station to request a solution from the Construction Department.

Suzhou 78

Armed assistance to collect field rent

Farmers in Xietang Chefang and other townships in Wuxian County have been making trouble over rent, and in the past month, incidents of gathering crowds to cause trouble, resisting officials and police, destroying township offices, and demolishing Baojia houses have occurred one after another, no less than a dozen times. County Magistrate Deng believes that although disputes have occurred repeatedly, he cannot give up eating because of choking, and the issue of urging rent should still be worked hard. On the morning of the 13th, he specially sent Zhang Yijun, a member of the Tenth District Handling Field Rent Disputes, and Li Zilian from the Ninth District to go to Lianmu Jin Temple and other townships in Xietang Township together with the district chiefs and primary school principals to persuade them to pay rent and check the rental conditions. At the same time, he sent the First Squadron of the Security Team to the township to be directed by the committee members to assist in the collection of rent and prevent everything to be thorough. According to those familiar with the field rent situation, the field rent problem in various townships in Wuxian County is very complicated. Strictly chasing the rent rice is the current palliative measure, not the fundamental solution. As for the fundamental solution, it is necessary to improve rural customs, strictly prohibit rural gambling, and ban the transfer of rent. Most of the farmers are lazy by nature. If they need fertilizer to cut grass, etc., they will order Jiangbei migrants to handle it on their behalf, spending money regardless of the cost. Moreover, there are gambling tables in the small tea houses in the countryside, which are shocking to the eye. Farmers often entrust farming to others and spend their good time in the small tea houses from morning to night. The government cannot ban it because its whip is too long. As for the transfer of field rent, this kind of bad habit that harms farmers should be strictly prohibited. If A has a rental field book and transfers it to B, and B transfers it to C, A and B will profit from it (called transfer fee). May I ask who is working hard to cultivate the field all year round, but after the autumn harvest, they have to bear the rent of the warehouse and pay the transfer fee to A and B who do not work for nothing. A and B are all powerful people in the countryside, so the villagers fear them like tigers and dare not resist. Such heavy exploitation is really too much for the poor farmers to bear, so various unfortunate events occur. However, as a result of the government's efforts to educate them over the years, the villagers no longer have the word "resist rent" in their mouths. The current situation is that although some people are deliberately making trouble, most of it is an economic problem.

Kong Xiangxi Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday to Discuss the Central Government's Handling of Guangdong and Guangxi, Decided to Focus on the Overall Situation 88
