Finance: Market Sentiment Weak; Gold Standard Continues Downward 167

The gold market struggled yesterday due to the continued decline in the benchmark gold price. With the swap period approaching, although there were many foreign buyers in the market, the settlement price was only 26.6 yuan, a difference of more than 10 yuan. The short sellers have no intention of settling, so they must wait until the end of the period. Otherwise, this swap will undoubtedly favor the short sellers. As a result, market sentiment was quite loose, leading to poor performance. In the morning, overseas silver markets saw London rising and the US holding steady. Forward silver prices rose by 5 to 20 basis points. Exchange rates remained high. London spot gold shrank by 2 pence. The Central Bank's official rates were announced, with both the British and US rates remaining unchanged. Customs gold unit fell by 2 basis points. The standard gold price fell to 1126.6 yuan. Over-the-counter preparatory trading opened at 38.00 yuan. Fuxing, Yongyuan, and Qianyichang took advantage of the low prices and moved up to 9 yuan. Dadecheng was still selling. The morning opening was slightly lower, but stabilized. The HSBC bank announced its official rates, with both British and US rates unchanged. At this time, the market stabilized somewhat due to Qianyuan's continued advances. However, selling pressure increased, ultimately leading to a decline. Although the silver balance tax did not move, there was a slight pullback. Later, due to the strengthening of the exchange rate, long positions were shaken and declined again. However, due to the continued strong buying interest from Qianyuan and others, the market managed to level off at noon. July contracts increased to over 15,000 lots. The July-August spread will begin next Monday, and it is predicted that the longs will pay around 5 yuan. The market situation for the first half of the day is recorded as follows:

The morning opening was 1138.8 yuan, down 0.2 yuan from the previous close. Fuxing, Yongyuan, Qianyichang, and Changxiang continued to buy, rising to 9.7 yuan. Dadecheng, Qiafeng, Shuiqing, Fayong supplied contracts at the high price. HSBC bank's rates were announced with British and US rates unchanged, and there were more buyers. Huixiang, Dadecheng, and Yicheng sold contracts, falling back to 8.1 yuan. Qianyuan and Daheng continued to buy, and the silver balance tax remained unchanged, rebounding to 8.8 yuan. Yicheng, Tongyi, Dadecheng, Dafa, and Yongzai sold again, falling to 7.7 yuan. Qianyuan, Chunyuan, and Yong maintained, rising to 8.4 yuan. The noon close was 1138.2 yuan.

The settlement price, based on the Central Bank's standard gold price, fell to 1126.6 yuan. In terms of the closing price, it was approximately 20 yuan weaker, a gain of about 1 yuan from the previous close. The registration for this month is 1134 yuan, and for July is 1138 yuan. The morning water supplement was 1134 yuan, with gold also increasing by 12 yuan, to 1150.8 yuan. The spot market remained stable, with Tianjin goods and 焓赤 both increasing by 15 yuan, with demand exceeding supply. There are still 336 contracts remaining for this month.

Trading in the market was relatively flat. In total, Qianyuan, Hengchang, Yongyuan, Changyong, Chunyuan, Yongdaheng, Fuyu, Hongkangyong, etc. were on the buying side. Fuxingyong, Dafayong, Shunfayong, Dadecheng, Shendayong, Qingfayong, Qiafengyong, Tongtaichang, Wumao, Yonghengyu, Yuxinxiang, etc. were on the selling side.

The market struggled in the first half of the day. The morning opening was 1138.8 yuan, and the noon close was 1138.3 yuan. The highest was 1139.7 yuan, and the lowest was 1137.7 yuan, with a fluctuation of 2.7 yuan. The result was a decrease of 0.7 yuan from the previous close. The total number of transactions was 7,119 contracts in the morning session.

The US Dollar Exchange Market Shows Signs of Loosening 168

The exchange market yesterday was characterized by persistent long positions in foreign exchange, leading to a mixed performance. The British pound remained flat, while the US dollar weakened slightly. Early morning overseas telegraphs indicated that the London market saw the pound rise to nearly 0.0625 for spot rates and 0.125 for forward rates. There were also reports that Indian buyers continued to purchase pounds after the market closed. The New York silver market was stable, while London forward silver prices rose by 0.005 to 0.02. London spot gold fell by 2.5 pence. The pound strengthened by 0.01 against the US dollar and rose by 15 points against the French franc. The US dollar was long at 0.05625 against the pound and short at 0.0625 against the French franc. The central exchange rate postings were unchanged for both the British pound and the US dollar, while the customs gold unit weakened. The exchange market opened in the morning with the near-term selling rate for the British pound at 1 shilling, 2 pence, and 73125, and the US dollar at 30.0625 yuan. These rates were flat compared to the previous close for both currencies. There was some interbank trading after the opening, but the market remained stable. Later, banks showed mixed activity. The HSBC bank kept its posted rates for both the British pound and the US dollar, as well as silver, unchanged, and the stamp duty remained the same. During this period, interbank trading was still prevalent, with many offers circulating. Subsequently, banks began to sell off, and while Chinese merchants were buying, the market gradually loosened. At the midday close, the near-term selling rate for the British pound was 1 shilling and 2 pence 375, and the US dollar was 30.09375 yuan, reflecting a flat British pound and a loosening US dollar by 0.03125 compared to the previous close. Forward rates for both the British pound and the US dollar were up by 0.0625. Chinese merchants bought approximately 100,000 US dollars. The flour market unexpectedly reversed course yesterday, with a sharp decline no less dramatic than the previous surge. Speculators and retailers were even more active. The previous surge was mainly driven by the political situation and public sentiment, and there was no real demand. Now that the political situation has stabilized and large players are selling, the high prices have no support, and the market has immediately reversed course. Large players are still holding on in the near-term market, so the decline is slower, but it is still less than 0.3 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price. The wheat market opened yesterday morning, already affected by the easing political situation and reports of lower prices for foreign wheat. News spread that new wheat was being shipped from various locations, and overseas and local players immediately rushed to liquidate. New short positions and traders were all eager to sell. The near-term market once fell to 4.33 yuan, down 0.12 yuan from the previous high. Children's Special

Ideals and Realization and its success 185

— Jun Peng

—Children Must Possess a Doer's Spirit—

In this publication. More than a dozen children have published the major question of "What will I be when I grow up?" Indeed, it is urgently needed to be examined, especially for ordinary children, who should pay attention to their own personal problems, so as to contribute to the country. After reading the aspirations of many children, I am very pleased. Some want to study science; some want to be great engineers; some want to be battlefield nurses; some want to run educational undertakings; These kinds of grand aspirations are indeed capable of saving the country and the people, and creating immeasurable blessings.

Our current ideal is the basis for future practice. Everyone at the end of the century has ideals, but success is very rare. What is the reason for this? It is the lack of a spirit of doing, working hard, and striving hard.

For example, if someone is called A to do something, but A does it carelessly and vaguely, and does not do it practically, of course it will not be good or successful. Also calling B to do it, initially very serious and practical, but encounters difficulties and cannot endure hardship, so give up halfway and do not go back to it. Also calling C to do it, is much better than A and B, and can break through these two difficulties, but when it is about to succeed, others say, "This thing will never succeed, what are you doing it for?" C becomes discouraged and does not continue. A failed because he did not do it practically, B failed because he lacked the spirit of working hard, and C failed because he lacked a strong will, so none of them succeeded.

Children! In the past, many people had this kind of aspiration, but how many succeeded? I hope you will quickly cultivate yourselves, so that you can achieve your own grand aspirations.

Wen Tianxiang in his Childhood 186

— Zou Xiao

In Luling County, Jiangxi Province, there is an ancestral hall in the school palace, which is dedicated to the great figures in the local area, such as Ouyang Wenzhong, Yang Zhongxiang, Hu Zhongjian, and Zhou Wenzhong, also known as the Ancestral Hall of the Four Gentlemen.

One day, Wen Tianxiang (who was not yet ten years old at the time), went to the ancestral hall to play, looking around, and listening to people saying that they were local sages, and he admired them very much! He said with emotion: "After I die in the future, I will not enjoy being worshipped in this ancestral hall like them, this is not a real great man!" Children, think about it, he had such a big ambition at such a young age. Naturally, it goes without saying that his father loved him very much. As the saying goes: "No one knows a son better than his father", and it is also said that "fathers hope their sons become dragons." Anyone would be happy to have this descendant, let alone his own father.

Sure enough, when he grew up, he did a lot of earth-shattering things for the Song Dynasty, trying to restore the Han Chinese state, and desperately resisting the Yuan soldiers, but the result was unfavorable, and he was captured. The Yuan Dynasty treated him especially well, wanting him to surrender. Emperor Yuan Shizu also persuaded him, and even asked him to be the prime minister, but he refused to the death. Like him, who supported the country, and like him, with such a spirit of patriotism, - he was not a loyal subject to a single family, he was indeed a patriot who supported the country and promoted the nation's ambitions. This spirit is a national revival pill. In short: His great personality is not only admirable and commendable, but also a model figure for children!

Living and Non-Living Things 187

— Zhen

Every morning, Min'er always goes to his family's garden alone to breathe some fresh air. The trees in the garden are already lush, looking out, a patch of lush green colors, which makes people pleasing to the eye, so he loves the trees very much, but he remembers his brother once said that those trees are living things, and they don't move at all, how can they be called living things?

"Brother, didn't you say that trees are living things the other day? How do you know that?"

"Yes, trees are living things. Why are they living things? Then we must compare them with non-living things to understand. Otherwise, it is too unfocused. There are many differences between living and non-living things: The material that makes up living things is extremely small cells, so small that we can't see them with the naked eye. They must be magnified under a microscope to see clearly. But non-living things do not have this. Living things always need to eat food, because food contains energy, and with energy, they can move, but part of the food is absorbed, so on the one hand, they need other food to replenish. If there is no food to replenish, will they not starve to death? You have never seen a stone eat food, because stone is a non-living thing and does not need it. Living things can grow, like a tree that can gradually grow up, but what about non-living ice? How can ice break a vase? Because water expands when it freezes, but this expansion is not growth, it can only increase in volume but will not grow. Living things can not only grow, but also produce small living things that look like themselves at a certain time. Non-living things cannot do this. If there is a stimulus from the outside, living things will respond to this stimulus and produce various movements. For example, if you hit a dog, the force of hitting it is the external stimulus. You see, that thing will definitely run away quickly, and that running away is a movement. Do you think non-living things can do this? Living things will die after a certain period of time, and trees will wither and die, but non-living things do not have the phenomenon of death. With such a comparison, you can know the differences between living and non-living things.

The Largest Electromagnet of Modern Times 189

— Dong Xun

Electromagnets can pick up iron objects. All of you children who have played with magnets know this! I think that children who play with magnets must have had this ideal: if small magnets can attract small iron objects, then if we make a large one, wouldn't we be able to attract all the enemy's weapons during war? Isn't that right?

The largest electromagnet in modern times weighs 1720 pounds. Its diameter is five feet two inches; its job is to lift and unload iron objects. It can lift 70,000 pounds of single, flat iron sheets. The picture shows the situation of a military magnet crane loading large pieces of iron into a freight car; it can load an average of 4,000 pounds each time!

This large magnet is entirely made of many thin copper sheets, wrapped on the outside with asbestos tape, and each coil is wrapped to act as a rope edge. Its movement is controlled by electric current.

As for the first electromagnet, it was made in 1828 by the American Jcseph Henry in Princetron; that electromagnet was U-shaped, made by bending an iron rod, and wrapped with many metal windings, the surroundings of which were wrapped with silk strips to serve as rope edges. (See left picture)

"The Last Lesson" 190

— Zhang Yuqing

Children! Perhaps you are unfamiliar with the term "The Last Lesson"? Now I will give you a general explanation.

"The Last Lesson" was originally a short story written by the French writer Daudet. The story is about: during the Franco-Prussian War in 1870, when the Prussian army invaded French territory, a French elementary school held "The Last Lesson" under enemy rule. But why is it "The Last Lesson"? Because after the enemy's fierce arrival, not only was the land annexed, but even the schools were taken over. So today a French teacher is teaching, and tomorrow an enemy teacher will come to teach! Today they are teaching French, and tomorrow they will be teaching Prussian! Today the teacher teaches the children to love France, but tomorrow the teacher will teach the children to love Prussia, recognizing the enemies who invade and oppress them as kind and loving protective envoys. The teacher solemnly finished this "Last Lesson." He was so heartbroken that he shed tears, and the students were also so moved that they burst into tears. Children, what a painful story this is!

But why is this story being brought to China now? Needless to say, it is because the national crisis is becoming more and more urgent, and the enemy army is driving straight in. Therefore, some people have borrowed the words "The Last Lesson," which is very appropriate.

Children! However, you don't need to resent, be ashamed, or even belittle yourselves just because you are overwhelmed by patriotic fervor. Why do I say this? Precisely because I have encountered children several times who have spoken to me in a tone that is resentful, ashamed, and belittling: "I only resent that I was born too young to follow the university students and middle school students to do national salvation work. Isn't this in vain for being Chinese? I am really ashamed! Alas! Children are too useless!" But, children! You must understand that saving the country does not rely on a moment's fervor, but on perseverance. The future of China needs you, the masters of the country!

Summer Hygiene 191

— Zong Lin

Recently, I have heard many doctors predict that Shanghai will have another epidemic year this year. Indeed, recalling this season four years ago, Shanghai experienced an epidemic. Many people died at that time, but fortunately, it was extinguished in a proper manner, so it did not spread.

Children! Do you still have that tragic scene imprinted in your minds? Do you feel scared? Maybe you will nod your heads to express your shock. But what's the use of just being afraid? We must take precautions to avoid the invasion of "seasonal diseases." The following are a few points that I want to contribute to you.

(1) Get Vaccinated. Each of you must have a "foresight" mentality and ask a doctor to inject you with a vaccine as early as possible to increase your resistance to disease and reduce your summer worries about the epidemic.

(2) Keep Your Home Clean. The rent in Shanghai is indeed surprisingly expensive! Most people cannot afford spacious housing. This is also one of the special circumstances of the city. Leaving aside the children who live in high-rise buildings, if you live in a pigeon-cage-like house every day because of the above situation, then, although the house is small, it is not very important. As long as the air is circulating, the dirt is removed, the appliances are adjusted, and mosquitoes and flies are eliminated, and everything is done thoroughly, you can also reduce the risk of being surrounded by disease.

(3) Be Careful About Your Diet. In addition to doing the first two things, we must also pay great attention to being careful about our diet. As the saying goes, "Disease enters through the mouth," which is true. If you don't pay attention to hygiene in your diet, disease will easily come to your door. Rotten food and things from street vendors are best not to buy at all. Because food is not clean, it often has bacteria, and I don't know how many thousands or tens of thousands of them are parasitic on it. Just think about it, how dangerous this is! So, for the sake of life safety, you must be careful about being clean in your diet.

Children! You are all the future masters of China. Now, in addition to enriching your studies, you must also exercise your bodies. Summer has arrived, and summer hygiene must first be paid attention to!

Proof of the Round Earth 192

— Qiu

The sun goes down in the west, slowly disappearing: the ground changes from pale yellow to twilight. Do you think the entire earth is shrouded in darkness? No: one half of the earth is experiencing night, and the opposite half is experiencing day.

The sun hangs high in the sky, shining on all directions. The Earth is round and constantly rotating there. The side facing the sun is day; the side facing away from the sun is night.

If you take a flight and rise 10,000 feet above the ground, you can see the sun set ten minutes later than on the ground.

The situation with the sun rising is the same. If you take a plane before sunrise and rise to a height of two miles above the ground, you can see the sun rise ten minutes earlier than on the ground.

The principle is the same as seeing the sunrise earlier and the sunset later on top of a high mountain than on the ground. This is clear evidence of the round earth.

The evidence of the round earth can also be explained by the different times in the east and west. In the east where we live, we see the sun earlier every day. For example, the time in Tokyo is a little more than an hour earlier than Shanghai; Honolulu is more than two hours earlier than Shanghai. In the west where we live, we see the sun later every day. For example, the time in Chengdu is a little more than an hour later than Shanghai; Yining in Xinjiang is two and a half hours later than Shanghai.

This is a simple and interesting proof of the round earth.

Dedicated to the 170,000 Boy Scouts Across the Country 193

Boy Scout brothers and sisters across the country! Long time no see. We believe that some readers, when they see our signature, will have an interesting memory from their Boy Scout life! That's right, in the past, we met many Boy Scout brothers from all over the place. Although we haven't had the opportunity to shake hands and chat happily, we have become close friends in spirit.

We have always hoped to have a few more gardens to give us more opportunities to stop, take a rest, and chat. In the past, we have opened such gardens in the Ta Kung Pao and Qingdao Morning Post; now we have even more enthusiastically gained the support of the editors of the Shen Bao "Children's Special Issue", who give us some valuable space every week. How happy and grateful should we be?

Here, we are willing to be your loyal friends and serve you sincerely. Here, you can ask questions, express opinions, and find new friends. Come on! Come on! We are willing to serve you!

Please pay special attention: we are willing to be lifelong friends with the children who write to us, so as long as you are not afraid of trouble, we are always prepared to chat with you for a long time. Although sometimes your questions may not be published here publicly—because many questions are limited to individuals, are not very important, or have already been answered publicly—we will still give you a satisfactory answer directly.

In addition, for children who are not yet Boy Scouts, we also welcome them to join.

We would like to dedicate this small "mailbox" to the 170,000 Boy Scout brothers across the country, and even more willing to dedicate it to all the children of the Republic of China at home and abroad.

Children who correspond, please follow the following guidelines:

Send your letters directly to: "China Boy Scout Self-Help Society, c/o Boy Scout Corps, Guangji Righteous School, Fude Lane, North Sichuan Road, Shanghai"

The questions in your letters should be as simple as possible.

Those who want to be introduced to friends must specify what kind of friends they want to make.

We also welcome children to discuss with us any opinions they have about Boy Scouting.

For the first correspondence, please write down the following points in detail: A. Name, native place, age; B. The China Boy Scout Troop × Team (or School) to which you belong (non-Boy Scouts do not need to write);

C. Qualification: elementary, intermediate, or advanced.

D. Position: Troop Leader, Squad Leader, Deputy Squad Leader, or various officers, etc.

E. Mailing address,

F. Permanent mailing address (can be omitted if there is none)

For children who have already corresponded with us, just write down the number we gave you in the second letter. This number is for your use for life, and you can communicate with us in the future without writing your name.

Here, we plan not to publish the letters, but only to announce the names of the writers and our replies.

Because there are only three of us doing this (Zhao Bangqian, Chen Guangxiang, Zheng Wuzhang), and at the same time the space here cannot be expanded, so please forgive us if there is some delay in time. We will never let you down.

Please, children, please shout "All men are brothers"!

Sincerely, China Boy Scout Self-Help Society

The Tale of the Righteous Dog (22) 195

They walked to Antwerp with great difficulty. At that time, the clock was striking ten times. Little Nanlo thought to himself, "If I had something on my body to sell, then I could buy bread for Padereshi to eat!" However, he only had a thin cloth coat and a pair of wooden shoes, so where could he exchange for money?

Padereshi understood Little Nanlo's meaning very well, put his nose in Little Nanlo's hand, as if begging him not to care about his pain.

The results of the painting competition were to be announced at noon this day. The place where the announcements will be is in a public building. Little Nanlo went toward that place. On the stone steps of the house and in the vestibule of the entrance, there were a large group of young people gathered, some of whom were of the same age as him, and some of whom were a little older. They were all accompanied by their parents and relatives. Little Nanlo squeezed into them, feeling very scared, and pulled Padereshi closer to his own body. All the large clocks in the city struck twelve times loudly, reporting that noon had arrived. The door of the inner hall suddenly opened; the many young people who had been waiting eagerly rushed in, as it was said that the winning book was placed on a high wooden platform.

A heavy fog seemed to rise before Little Nanlo's eyes, covering his eyes. His head was dizzy, and his hands and feet seemed to be paralyzed. When his eyes were clear, he saw that the book placed on the high place was not his own work! At that moment, a commotion called out the name of the winner, he was called Stephen, the son of a wharf owner in Antwerp.

When Little Nanlo regained consciousness and slowly woke up, he was lying on the stone outside the door. Padereshi was guarding by his side and had used all kinds of methods to wake him up. A large group of young people shouted in the distance, celebrating the victory of their friend Stephen, and they all crowded around him and returned to his home.

A Visit to the National Children's Painting Exhibition 196

— Ji Ping

The National Children's Painting Exhibition, after four or five months of preparation, officially opened on June 6. Such a grand children's book exhibition is the first in our country, so everything about the conference is worth reporting to the children who love to read this publication. The exhibition was initiated by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee. Because it was held at the Shanghai Municipal Stadium, it was also entrusted to five groups including the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau to be responsible for the preparations. They spent a lot of time and effort to have such a satisfactory harvest, so naturally they should be grateful.

When I arrived at the venue yesterday, there were thousands of children lined up to visit. Everyone felt very happy. One child said to the teacher, "We children can actually do so well and decorate such a big venue like a sky full of stars! Ah, the power of children is really great." A child wearing a green shirt said, "Mom! I love to see the works of children from the four northeastern provinces the most! It's a pity that the four northeastern provinces have been temporarily occupied by others. I don't know when they will be recovered!" A Boy Scout said, "Dad! Don't think that fine arts are not as good as science. Building houses requires drawings, building machines requires drawings, and building airplanes and cannons also requires drawings. The use of drawings is very important." I think their words all make sense.

The conference's products were based on provinces and cities as units, with a total of 28 units and a quantity of more than 30,000 pieces. Even remote provinces and regions had products. One-third of them were reviewed and selected. Among them, they were divided into eight groups: brush, pencil, colored pencil, watercolor, charcoal, pattern, etc. There were also more than 160 children who were wielding brushes in front of guests, painting very vividly. Some of them were from Chahar, and their spirit was truly admirable. This time, Shanghai had the largest number of participants, with more than 1,000 people, and Zhejiang had 1,500 people. Colored pencils were the most common, accounting for 42%, followed by watercolors, and pencils were the least common. Scenery was the most common theme, accounting for 40%, followed by people, and animals were the least common. The free surface works of children aged 14 to 10 were the most interesting. Many senior students expressed national ideas and had a strong patriotic spirit, but some were instructed or embellished by adults, which inevitably lost their pure creativity.
