Supplemental Local Edition of Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Chronicles of Books and Newspapers

Review of Ms. Liu Wang Liming's "Waves of Life" 197

— Hu

——Published by the China Women's Production Cooperative, 205 Yuanmingyuan Road, priced at $1.20 per copy——

"Waves of Life" is a full-length novel that has just been published recently. Its author is Ms. Liu Wang Liming, whom we are familiar with. On the opposite page of this novel, we see these lines of poetry:

"Forward! Little boat of life, forward!

Do not fear the waves in the sea,

Do not fear the frightening waves in the river,

Throughout the ages, only the selfless,

Loyal, brave, and hardworking will triumph—

This is the law of creation,

This is our life."

At first glance, such lines of poetry seem very progressive, but upon careful consideration, they are extremely empty and devoid of any real content. Therefore, their meaning is also not definite: you can use it to express truly progressive ideas, or you can say it is a pleasant song for those who retreat; the so-called "loyalty," "courage," and "hard work," the so-called "selflessness," these words do not necessarily have progressive meaning, and their meaning must be judged by their specific content. If such lines of poetry can express the entire content of "Waves of Life," then in reality its specific content may not be progressive; the words "forward," "loyalty," and "courage" are just beautiful decorations.

First, in terms of the subject matter of this novel, it is merely the ordinary love life of young men and women. Although the author has raised many significant real-world issues in the construction and development of the story, these have not been portrayed as important themes, and of course, have not been accurately expressed; instead, they are raised incidentally and distortedly expressed. Naturally, the evaluation of literary works cannot be based solely on the subject matter, but the subject matter is closely related to the value of the work. If the value of a work must be determined by its power to move people, then works that artistically depict typical social phenomena that are deeply related to the majority of people should be the most valuable, because this can resonate deeply with the majority of people; as for personal trivial matters and special life experiences, they are of interest only to the individual and cannot generate empathy among the majority of people who live differently. Although "Waves of Life" was produced in the current turbulent era of China, it is not a depiction of the typical social phenomena of this era; it only expresses the experiences of a woman who rebels against arranged marriages in old families, especially her special love life: this is a fashionable theme since the "May Fourth" Movement; but because the "May Fourth" era has long passed, such a theme has already lost its progressive significance.

Looking at the ideological content of this novel again, the author first expresses a protest against the feudal parental arranged marriage system. She tells us that there is a young woman named Huang Muyun who ran away from home to resist arranged marriages, and at the same time, the young man Renbang, who was engaged to her, also left home because he was dissatisfied with the arranged marriage; later, after many twists and turns, they ingeniously fell in love freely and became husband and wife. In this way, although this young couple had simultaneously resisted arranged marriages, they eventually came together, but in form they always went through a period of resistance to the feudal family. Needless to say, this kind of thinking is also the thinking of the "May Fourth" era, which is already a thing of the past; but the author does not express even this kind of anti-feudal thinking of the "May Fourth" era very thoroughly: she does not use the opposite of this thinking to replace the old feudal thinking, but another form of virtuous doctrine. She strives to praise Huang Muyun, the heroine, for her obedience to her husband after marriage. In her writing, when Muyun discovers that her husband Renbang has fallen in love with someone else, and feels that such family life is tasteless, she leaves the family, but this is not "Nora's departure," nor is it a thorough rebellion against the ugly family life, but rather to promote the repentance of a husband who is unfaithful to her emotions; the fact is that after Muyun leaves home, although her husband is living with a romantic woman, and although she has another man who loves her very much asking for her hand, she remains absolutely faithful to her married husband, and as a result, her husband does repent and takes her back home. How much more progressive can you say that such a spirit of "loyalty" and "courage," such an idea of "remaining faithful to one's husband until death," such obedience to men, and such a doctrine of virtue are compared to those who completely obey parental arranged marriages? But this is precisely the theme of this novel, precisely the central idea of the author; the novel's Ms. Huang Muyun is precisely the author's incarnation.

"Waves of Life" was produced from the "×××" to the "×××" era, and the author also expresses the situation of these two major events in the middle. However, she initially adopts a satirical attitude, completely negating the debates among the masses caused by these two major events, and then openly expresses that the young couple Renbang and Muyun, whom she praises, are "rightists," advocating "studying hard and striving to become stronger." Readers certainly know whether this claim is correct based on past and present circumstances, and we do not need to say more. However, judging from this point alone, we can also know what the author's position is in the current national liberation movement.

In this novel, the author also expresses the suffering of the hard-working, and many dark sides of society, but this is not to arouse everyone's resistance and seek liberation with their own strength, but to promote Christian dogma, to ask people to believe in God, to promote universal love, and to encourage people to donate money to run religious charities. The heroine Huang Muyun, portrayed by the author, is a Christian. She is enthusiastic about charity, has the spirit of "sacrificing for the cause," and has extreme faith in God. As long as there are any disasters or pains, "Indeed, heaven and man are in harmony, the wind and waves subside, and the radiance of the sun slowly shoots out from the clouds." Reading this novel cannot help but remind us of Tolstoy. This great genius writer did his best to expose the hypocrisy and darkness of Russian society at that time, but he also asked everyone to believe in God in order to prevent thorough resistance at home and maintain the status of the feudal aristocracy, thus damaging the value of many of his great works. "Waves of Life" should be given the same evaluation for expressing the dark side of society while simultaneously promoting Christian dogma. Of course, I am not saying that the author of "Waves of Life" can be compared with Tolstoy; what I mean is the intention of Christians to expose the dark side of society.

As for the artistic expressiveness of this novel, it is also very low. For the development of events and the expressions of characters, the author only narrates abstractly, and cannot be said to portray them concretely. However, the main characteristic of literary works lies in concrete, vivid, and artistic expression. If you want to express that something is very serious, or that a situation is very tense, or that someone is very painful, these cannot be expressed by certain abstract words or certain simple lists of facts, but must delve into the core of the event and the hearts of the characters, and depict them concretely and vividly from all aspects. The events and characters depicted in a work must make people feel as if real events and living characters appear before their eyes, that is good, otherwise it is an inferior product; and "Waves of Life" belongs to the latter in terms of artistic expression. Just to give an example, such as Muyun being imprisoned at home, her grandfather wanting to bury her alive because she resisted marriage, and her mother being forced to death, how tense should this section be, and what should the various scenes in this section be like, but in the author's writing, in addition to Muyun's simple crying, many necessary scenes, such as the grandfather's tyrannical posture, the kind mother's inner contradictions, Muyun's painful and angry psychology and expressions, and the intricate relationships between family members and relatives in this incident, have not been concretized; therefore, in this section of facts, there is no climax or culmination of excitement, tension, grief, or anger, no living scenes, and no living characters: all that is there is flat confession and narration. – This is the author's lack of artistic expressiveness.

Because of the author's low artistic expressiveness, the structure of this work is not rigorous, and the handling and arrangement of many events are inappropriate. I think that many unimportant things in the middle should be omitted in order to concentrate on depicting those important scenes. However, the author lists all the trivial things; sometimes even deliberately trying to make the event tortuous, leading to many unnecessary things, so the result makes people feel that the novel is just a pile and list of facts, and this pile and list is very scattered, almost completely without artistic meaning. As for the portrayal of typical characters, it is even more impossible to talk about being vivid and profound. Muyun and Renbang, as well as all the characters in the entire novel, have no personality and do not seem to be living people; after reading this novel, we cannot develop a vivid impression of all the expressions of the characters in the middle, their attitudes in talking and doing things, their inner and outer selves, and the main characteristics of their personalities. I think that even the author probably cannot specifically tell us what the personalities of Muyun and Renbang are.

However, the author's personal thoughts, what kind of attitude she has toward life, and what she hopes for can be seen in this work (as already said, the protagonist Huang Muyun is the author herself; as for who plays the male role, we still don't know), although there is her own defense and excessive exaggeration in the middle.

Social Science Lecture

Critique of Malthus' Theory of Population 198

— Ling Xian

The population problem is a very complicated issue. However, among the scholars of the bourgeoisie, the scholar who is revered as the authority on the theory of population is Malthus. In Europe in the 17th and 18th centuries, because of the rise of modern nation-states, the special development of commercial capitalism, and the enrichment and strengthening of the country, the acquisition of overseas colonies became the most common demands of various countries, so at that time, various countries competed to promote population growth as a policy, which was entirely in order to establish a strong army, to travel and immigrate, and even to increase the population in order to increase consumption and expand the domestic market. However, at the same time in the 18th century, industrial

Page 20

Capitalism also developed rapidly, so because of its concentration and destructive effects, a large layer of poor proletarians was gradually created in the lower classes of society, and even gradually manifested as a surplus of labor, and an industrial reserve army of unemployment was constantly discovered. As a result, the increase in population became a labor bulge phenomenon that capitalism could not digest, and even the poor relief laws and other measures that had been advocated in the past to compensate for the shortcomings of the population increase policy still became useless and harmful policies. Therefore, abandoning the policy of increasing the population could not but become a new attempt of capitalist production, and Malthus' theory of population arose from this attempt. His theory of the population problem was published at the beginning of the 19th century, and the core of his theory was to oppose the policy of increasing the population, and advocating birth control was a prominent proof.

According to the main points of Malthus' theory of population, first, he believes that according to the natural fertility rate of human beings, it increases geometrically, such as 1:2; 2:4; 4:8; 8:16; 16:32. However, the increase in food, even if human productivity is advancing, its rate of advance can only increase according to arithmetic progression, that is, according to an arithmetic progression such as 1:2:3:4:5:6:7:8. Therefore, comparing the rate of food increase with the rate of population increase, the former is always unable to catch up with the latter. Second, but why has mankind experienced so many years of history, and there is still no problem of overcrowding on the earth? In his view, this is because when the increase in food and population is slightly out of balance, there is a disharmony between production and consumption, between needs and supplies, so survival competition, the law of the jungle, and the survival of the fittest occur among human beings themselves, and famines, wars, killing the old and abandoning the young, etc. restrict their suppression, and too many people are eliminated, and even defensive restrictions are carried out due to poverty, etc., so that the population cannot increase according to its natural rate of increase. Third, because the population increases faster than food, and because all the poverty and evils of society arise from this, facilities such as poor relief laws and increased wages actually promote population growth and the occurrence of social evils, so to save society's morbid state, only the implementation of early marriage correction and birth control is a proper and possible way.

Malthus' theory of population not only shows that capitalist production replaces labor with its machine production, and creates social poverty and unemployment with its concentration and destruction of small production, and attempts to suppress the increase in population because it cannot digest the excess labor, as we have already mentioned above, but it also has a role in concealing the contradictions of this production system. Because the wars, poverty, and excessive labor of some people and the unemployment of others to the point of having nothing to do, and even the evils of malnutrition in capitalist society, are entirely caused by the contradictions of the system itself. However, Malthus attributed this cause to the balance between population increase and food increase, and as a result of this survival competition, this is entirely to make everyone unable to see the defects of capitalist production under the cover of this theory, and to shift the target to the natural law of human reproduction, where they want to find a way of salvation, how clever and cheap is this?

In Malthus' theory of the population problem, there are many fundamental errors that we must point out. The first is that his theory that the population increases according to geometric progression, while food increases according to arithmetic progression, and the increase in food cannot keep up with the increase in population, is not entirely correct. Naturally, if we talk about the purely natural law of population increase, it should indeed be very fast, but human beings are not simply subject to natural laws like ordinary organisms, so in terms of reproduction, they are also subject to social laws. The development of productive forces, social relations of production and their systems, etc., all specifically dominate the increase or decrease of population and human reproduction. For example, in primitive ethnic groups where production is young, the fact of killing the old and abandoning the young is common because they cannot support a large population. In patriarchal and feudal societies, under the production form of patriarchal system and agricultural economy, due to the prosperity of large families and the need for extensive labor in farming, and the lifelong gathering of the two sexes without separation, etc., there is a demand for many children and grandchildren, which affects the population growth. However, in the lower masses of capitalist society, because of poverty and the inability to marry, as well as the destruction of ten families and the necessity for the two sexes to make a living separately, etc., all of which are sufficient to affect the low decline of the population fertility rate. Therefore, unless there are natural disasters, wars, etc. that massively destroy the population in the past agricultural economic society, and modern capitalist countries encourage reproduction due to special relationships, such as Italy, the general fertility rate in the lower classes, the productivity of capitalist society is lower than that of the past agricultural economic society. Here I will only give a few examples from before and after the Great War to prove this. In 1908, the population productivity rate was 33.7 in Japan; 26.6 in the United States; 26.2 in Norway; 25.7 in Sweden; 28.6 in Denmark; 29.7 in the Netherlands; 24.9 in Belgium; 20.1 in France; 33.7 in Italy; 32.0 in Germany; but in 1918, Japan was 32.2; the United Kingdom was 17.5; Norway was 25.8; Sweden was 20.1; Denmark was 24.2; the Netherlands was 25.3; Belgium was 9.5; France was 10.0; Italy was 19.0 in 1917; and Germany was 26.5 in 1914. The simple numbers tell us that the further capitalist society develops, the lower the population fertility rate becomes. There is not a single country in Europe or even Japan whose population fertility rate in 1918 was not lower than in 1908. Although the European war passed in the middle, this has little to do with the war's death toll, because this is in terms of the productivity rate of every thousand living people. From this, we can see that the productivity rate of population increase cannot be explained according to the natural law of biology, it is dominated by social laws, and it expresses its progress and retreat according to the changing laws of productive forces and relations of production. Of course, Malthus also said that the increase in population is restricted by the economic and productive restrictions of food, but he always regards the natural law of population reproduction as the theme. In fact, it is only an abstract concept, not the concrete law of population change. Only by explaining population change based on the changes in productive forces and relations of production can it be a concrete and truly applicable law. Malthus' law is a useless abstract law, not the real law of human reproduction.

As for whether the increase in food can keep up with the increase in population? Here Malthus is still trapped in the mud pit of abstract comparison errors. First, the increase in food itself is not always limited to an unchanging arithmetic progression. In the more forward advance of productive forces, its rate of increase is greater, and it may even jump from arithmetic progression to geometric progression. If you take a look at the progress of modern agricultural and industrial production, you will know that using the same labor and the same land as before to produce can now obtain many times higher products. Second, even taking the comparison between population increase and food increase, the productive efficiency of a person's labor now exceeds the amount he can consume by many times because he has the help of science and technology. That is to say, his productivity is several times higher than his fertility rate, because in terms of the number of people that his productivity can support, it is absolutely impossible for his fertility to catch up. Now a worker's product can support dozens or hundreds of people, but is his fertility that great? In fact, it is lower. If his production is used to support all his children, it cannot be consumed, not to mention that his children will continue to produce. It is a pity that in the current society, his surplus production has turned against the capitalist to increase capital and support many parasites, so he and the general hard-working people are still in poverty, but this is by no means because their production volume is not enough to support them.

Secondly, because of that fundamental premise error, Malthus attributed the useless consumption of the population to the survival competition caused by insufficient food, wars, poorness, poor treatment, etc., and attributed all the evils of society to insufficient food, and regarded the loss of population as the natural law of the survival of the fittest. To be honest, his theory is entirely just to cover up the evils of the social system. Because the root cause of all wars and poverty, everyone can now understand that it is the contradiction in the capitalist relations of production, not due to insufficient food, nor is it dominated by any natural law of human survival competition. If you say that this is the inevitable result of insufficient food, then why do the current milk and coffee kings pour these things into the sea, and store wheat in warehouses to listen? If you say this is survival competition, then is it that without this war and the exploitation and oppression of capital, human beings cannot survive? And are the current hard-working masses naturally inferior, so they should naturally be punished by poverty, unable to marry and have children, malnutrition, overwork, etc., in order to consume their lives and the right to transmit their species and be eliminated? In fact, the civilization of modern society is created by the hard-working masses, and in terms of their achievements, they are precisely the best for survival, and should not be the inferior who are eliminated by survival competition. Therefore, it is completely incorrect to attribute all social evils to the survival competition caused by insufficient food, and to regard the loss of population among the hard-working masses as the inferior who are eliminated in survival competition. These evils should be borne by the social system itself, and are the result of the existing relations of production.

Since social poverty, wars, and all evils are not due to the rapid increase in population and the slow increase in food, but to the result of social relations of production, then the fundamental solution to this problem is not what Malthus proposed to restrict early marriage and childbirth, etc., that can be effective (although early marriage should be restricted), but to transform the social relations themselves. Many birth control advocates today are probably based on Malthus's theory and the method of solving poverty, which we dare not agree with in the slightest.

Biography of a Famous Person

Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov 199

— Nan

Anyone who pays attention to the international situation almost certainly knows the famous name of the Red diplomat Litvinov. He is the main executor of the Soviet Union's peaceful diplomacy in recent years; even if we don't acknowledge the success of Soviet peaceful diplomacy in recent years, Litvinov can be said to be the practical figure representing this success.

Litvinov's appearance is quite similar to that of a wealthy merchant. His face is round and plump, his belly protrudes, and his gait is naturally not very agile. He really resembles a corpulent businessman. Indeed, strangely enough, this Red diplomat did not come from an impoverished family. His father could be considered a wealthy man of his time, and he himself aspired to become a great entrepreneur during his youth. However, he was later influenced by the intellectual currents of the time and dedicated himself to the revolution. As a result, in 1910, he was arrested by the Tsarist government and exiled to the desolate Siberia, where he first tasted the bitterness of revolution and at the same time strengthened his conviction.

In the Russian revolutionary movement, one of Litvinov's main contributions can be attributed to his assistance in economic affairs. He had worked as a bookseller, as a draftsman for an architect, and as a traveling salesman. His talent at that time could be said to be the same as his talent in diplomacy now. He was able to use many methods to achieve victory and the goal of making money. However, he did not put the money he earned into his own pocket, but used it to support the revolution. What is generally known now is that Gorky provided economic assistance to the Russian revolution at that time, but few people know that Litvinov also made a significant economic contribution to the past Russian revolution. If one were to "assess merits and award prizes" now, then the diplomat Litvinov and the writer Gorky should be mentioned in the same breath.

In 1918, after the success of the Russian Revolution, Litvinov was in London, and Moscow telegraphed to appoint him as the ambassador to England. When this news spread, the British, knowing that a former traveling peddler had become an ambassador, were understandably astonished. But this was only the beginning of Litvinov's activities in the diplomatic world, and his remarkable performance was yet to come.

Litvinov's appearance on the international diplomatic stage, playing an important role, was at the Fourth World Disarmament Conference in November 1929. The fact is that while the great powers were arguing endlessly in the conference, Litvinov, on behalf of the Soviet Union, dropped a surprising bombshell. He proposed to immediately implement complete disarmament, completely abolishing the army, navy, and air force. Although this astonishing proposal was rejected, the name of the new diplomat Litvinov was deeply noted by the great powers. By 1930, he officially became the Soviet Foreign Minister, frequently traveling between important cities such as London, Paris, and Geneva, working hard on the Soviet Union's peaceful diplomatic activities.

After becoming the official Foreign Minister, in 1931 and 1932, Litvinov, based on the Soviet Union's peace policy, signed treaties of non-aggression with neighboring countries such as Poland, Finland, Latvia, Estonia, and Lithuania, building a secure defense line around the Soviet Union. Then, at the London World Economic Conference in 1933, he further demonstrated his diplomatic skills, seeing through the internal panic and mutual contradictions of the great powers, often defeating Germany's attacks, and signing multilateral agreements with Turkey and Afghanistan, gaining Spain's recognition of the Soviet Union, as well as the pro-Russian sentiments of countries such as Britain, the United States, and France.

People say that 1933 to 1934 was Litvinov's diplomatic year, and this is indeed not an exaggeration. During this period, this new diplomat was busy on diplomatic journeys almost every day, leaving many important records in the history of Soviet diplomacy. Among them, what is particularly worth mentioning are the . The former, from the current perspective, although has no decisive effect on the international situation, is somewhat related to the development and changes of the Far East situation. As for the latter, it can be said to be a key to the transformation of the recent European and even world situation. We know that before Hitler came to power, the Soviet Union was close to Germany in resisting France, while France at that time was the organizer of the anti-Soviet front; conversely, since Hitler came to power, not only did German-Russian relations deteriorate, but the contradictions between Germany and France also became more acute, which promoted the rapprochement between France and the Soviet Union; and Litvinov was one of the intermediaries for the rapprochement between France and the Soviet Union. Due to the development of the friendly relations between France and the Soviet Union, great changes have taken place in the European and even the world situation. We only need to look at the recent debates within France regarding the Franco-Soviet pact, and Hitler's tearing up the Locarno Treaty and marching troops into the Rhineland on the pretext that France would ratify this pact, to imagine the relationship between Franco-Soviet intimacy and the European and world situation.

When the Soviet Union was invited to join the League of Nations, Litvinov declared that he was a representative of a new country in the world, and at the same time, he explicitly stated the Soviet Union's pacifism. This is because the Soviet Union exists in the real capitalist society and must still have necessary relations with various capitalist countries, and cannot completely detach itself from the national relations of this world. Based on this principle, the Soviet Union has been working hard on internal construction and at the same time using the contradictions between capitalist countries to ensure its own security: and Litvinov is the executor of this security-guaranteeing peaceful diplomacy. Now, as the international situation becomes increasingly tense, his diplomatic work is naturally becoming more tense. He is now an old man over sixty years old, but he still maintains the active spirit of youth in his diplomatic work, and he is fighting for the security of the Soviet Union and the real peace of the world.

Amateur Studies

How to Study International Politics? 200

— Lisheng

Since you live in the real world, you cannot but pay attention to the political situation of this world. Because whether you like it or not, changes in international politics are bound to affect your country, and thus inevitably affect your life. For example, the currency war triggered by the political struggle between Britain, Japan, and the United States for markets in the Pacific directly affected China's monetary policy, and thus affected the lives of all Chinese people. Also, the dynamics of European politics, which are farther away from us, are also closely related to us; in fact, political events such as the pro-Japanese and pro-German development resulting from the conflict between Germany, France, and Russia are directly related to the liberation of the Chinese people. As for the outbreak of a world war and changes in the Far East situation, they will even more strongly affect the lives of everyone. Therefore, if you do not want to live muddleheadedly, and you are living during this period when the world crisis is developing, you should earnestly pay attention to changes in the domestic and international political situation in order to determine your attitude towards life; the motto of "not talking about current affairs" will not be accepted by a living person, except for a muddleheaded fool who is content with ignorance.

So, how do you study international politics? Now we are going to talk to you about this issue.

First of all, you should know that the economy is the foundation of society, and certain political forms or political changes arise from a certain economic foundation; we can say that the development and changes of international politics follow the development and changes of the international economy. In broad terms, the war crisis currently manifested by international political relations is guided by the crisis of world economic development. Because in the development of the world economy, all capitalist countries have experienced contradictions of overproduction and inability to sell, and under these contradictions, they have to desperately compete for markets, so the problem of redivision of colonies and wars for markets has become increasingly realistic. In terms of partial international political dynamics, such as Italy's invasion of Abyssinia, it is clearly also caused by the development of the internal economic crisis in Italy; we must understand the phenomena of Italy's lack of raw materials, overpopulation, national impoverishment, unemployment panic, trade shrinkage, and financial crisis in order to understand Mussolini's adventurous act of invading East Africa. Furthermore, when it comes to the foreign policy of each country, it is even more necessary to explain it in terms of its economic situation? Here we can cite a clear example. The outward aggression of Italy, Germany, and their fellow travelers in the East often takes military force as the vanguard, using military and political aggression to assist and develop economic aggression, but the United States is conducting economic aggression "peacefully" without first taking military risks. What is the reason for this? Are they not all imperialists? Why are their methods of aggression different? This is because The United States’ situation means that it cannot engage in "peaceful" competition with other imperialists, so it has to take military risks; while the United States, because its financial power is too great, can control North America and can invade the colonies or exclusive markets of other imperialists without first engaging in military competition. Based on these, we should be able to think that if we do not understand the situation of the world economy and the general situation of the economies of various countries, we cannot understand the complicated international political relations and the political dynamics of various countries.

Secondly, you should pay attention to the history and content of international treaties, especially those important international treaties that have been produced since the last world war; such as the Treaty of Versailles, the Kellogg-Briand Pact, the Locarno Treaty, etc. Because although treaties cannot absolutely bind the actions of the great powers, generally speaking, there is a close relationship between them and the internal and external affairs of the treaty countries; moreover, we can even say that the formal structure of international relations is based on international treaties as a clue. Therefore, every new event that occurs in the international community will arouse public opinion in various countries to evaluate and discuss certain treaties. Don't we often see news in the newspaper that a certain country accuses a certain country of violating the spirit of a certain treaty? That can be said to be the concrete struggle of the provisions of international politics. More specifically, such as Germany's rearmament in the past, the French recognized as a violation of the Versailles Treaty; recently, Germany's abolition of the Locarno Treaty and the deployment of troops into the Rhineland has aroused a struggle of international faith, which is not only a superficial treaty issue, but also a manifestation of the sharp intensification of the political interests of Germany and France at the root. Because the Treaty of Versailles and the Locarno Treaty are tools used by France to ensure its victories in the last world war and to control Europe, it must maintain these two treaties; conversely, in Germany's view, these two treaties are binding on Germany's development, so it is always trying to lift them. In this way, in the Treaty of Versailles and the Locarno Treaty, Germany and France have an irreconcilable political conflict. From this point of view, if we study international politics without knowing the history and content of important international treaties, then not only will we be unable to sort out a clue to the complicated international relations, but even the words of what treaty is printed on the newspaper every day may not be understood, and in practice become a blind person who cannot even understand the newspaper.

Moreover, from a horizontal perspective, the world's geographical situation is also something that students of international politics should pay attention to. Because the national defense of various countries in the world and the ways in which they develop outward are directly related to their geographical situation, certain important places often become the goals of great power struggles and become the center of international political problems. Such as the Mediterranean problem, the Danube River basin problem, the Balkan problem, the Memel problem, the Pacific problem, etc., are currently the. the problem , and we don’t understand the world's shape , don’t know the location of various important places in the world and their political, economic, or military functions, then we cannot understand the dynamics of international politics. Let's take a recent example. For example, the problem of Italy's use of violence to occupy Abyssinia, although this is caused by the internal reasons why Italy must invade outward, but here the question is why Italy did not march into the Balkans or other places, but must embark on an expedition to East Africa? The reason is that the situation in the Balkans or other places is too complicated, and Britain, France, and other countries have strong forces there, making Mussolini afraid to act rashly in those places; as for Abyssinia, although it also has a deep stake in countries such as Britain and France, their direct power there is not very great; and Abyssinia is connected to Italian Eritrea and Somaliland, and swallowing Abyssinia can make Italy's colonies in Africa into one piece; therefore, Mussolini chose this weak country—Abyssinia—that would not encounter extremely strong resistance as the object of his outward aggression. Although our explanation cannot be used to fully explain the relationship between Italy's invasion of Abyssinia and the geographical situation, it can be clearly seen in the middle that this problem does have a great relationship in the geographical situation. Therefore, if you do not understand Italy's position in Europe and in the world, and do not know the terrain of Abyssinia, then you cannot understand the entirety of the problem.

In addition, five-sixths of the countries on the Earth today have many classes, and even many groups in these classes. They each have political parties and political spokespersons, who often stand on their positions to express or even implement certain political views; therefore, a change in a country's cabinet, the turnover of administrative personnel, will affect it's internal and external affairs that are moving: This is not only directly related to the internal politics of its own country, but also has a greater or lesser impact on the world situation. For example, in Germany before Hitler came to power, German-Soviet relations were very good, while Franco-Soviet relations were deteriorating, but after Hitler came to power, because the groups he represented and the policies he pursued were different, German-Soviet relations deteriorated, and the contradictions between Germany and France became more acute, which also promoted the rapprochement between France and the Soviet Union, changing the European situation. Another example is the result of the recent French general election, where the left-wing People's Front won a great victory, and the Socialist Party rose to form a cabinet, which is bound to have a great impact on the European situation. Therefore, when we study international politics, we must know what groups the political parties and politicians of the major countries in the world represent and what their political views are; otherwise, we will not only be unable to understand certain changes that occur in international politics, see the trends in the international situation, but also be at a loss for the political changes in the major countries.

In addition, studying international politics naturally requires actual "study," and requires regular reading of books and newspapers; moreover, when studying, it must be particularly attentive and not sloppy. For example, some people just glance at the international news in the newspaper and only look at the title; but they do not know that the entire content of political news cannot be displayed in a few words of the title, and sometimes the truth of certain news cannot even be seen in the surface words that record it. It is necessary to carefully study and understand its "meaning beyond the words" to understand its essence. If necessary, you can even subscribe to several newspapers and magazines to read; I think that in the current China, such as "Shen Bao," "Shen Bao Weekly," "Ta Kung Pao," "Shishi Xinbao," "Damei Evening News," "World Knowledge," etc., those who study international politics need to subscribe to them regularly.

Life Guidance

How to Hire a Maid 201

— Lunyan

Hiring a maid is not an easy task. The "辍耕录" says it well: "When a maid first comes, she is called a 'beaded abacus,' meaning she moves without being pushed. After a while, she is called a 'counting abacus,' meaning she moves when pushed. After a long time, she is called a 'Buddha's head bead,' meaning she is always still, and does not move even when pushed." This is a good description of a maid. Then how can a maid always be like a "beaded abacus," moving without being pushed? Let me tell you.

Before going to a matchmaker to call for a nanny, first, you must decide what kind of person you like to use. For example, if you like Suzhou nannies, then go to the "Suzhou Matchmaker Shop." If you like strong Anhui nannies, then go to the "Jinling Matchmaker Shop." Otherwise, you will never find a satisfactory nanny. Second, you must understand the situation of your own family and what age of maid is appropriate. For example, if your family lives in a three-story building, and there are children studying at school who need to have lunch delivered, or there are many letters coming and going, and you often have to go to the post office to send letters, then you must use a strong maid who is between twenty-two or three years old and thirty-five years old, otherwise she will not be able to do the job happily.

After deciding on your own ideas, you can go to the matchmaker shop to choose. At this time, you can carefully observe which one has the neatest clothes—not gorgeous—the most dignified attitude, the most peaceful demeanor, and the strongest body. That one should be selected. Because those who cannot even clean their own clothes will not do things cleanly, those with a frivolous attitude and reckless behavior are prone to cause trouble, and those with a weak body cannot do anything at all. In order to avoid future disputes, you must be stricter at the beginning.

After the maid is selected, she must first do a trial run for three days. During these three days, the maid is at her most hardworking, that is, the so-called "beaded abacus." However, because "newcomers are slow and do not know the pots and pans," the housewife must tell her in detail what she should do every day. But you must be adaptable. For example, if the maid comes at nine in the morning, which is the time to pick and wash vegetables and prepare lunch, you must tell her how to distribute the vegetables and how many liters of rice to measure. If she comes at two or three in the afternoon—which is rare, most come in the morning—, then tell her to wash clothes and cook dinner. Before going to bed, tell her what time to get up tomorrow, and after getting up, first start the coal stove and cook porridge, and then clean up the living room, so that she will not be at a loss after getting up.

After three days of work, if both the master and the servant are satisfied, then it is time to "set the wages." After the wages are set, it must be done for at least one month. Neither party can "terminate the contract," otherwise, they will have to compensate for the loss—if the master takes the initiative, the master will pay an extra month's wages, and if the servant takes the initiative, one month's wages will be deducted.

During the first month, the housewife should be particularly careful in handling the household affairs and pay attention to all the actions of the maid. Because the first month is the best period for the housewife to test the maid. If the housewife handles the household affairs in an orderly manner, then the maid will know that the housewife is very shrewd and will not dare to cheat. "People's hearts are different, each is like their face." How can you know whether this maid is honest or cunning in the short three-day trial period? Therefore, the housewife should test her at any time and anywhere—but be careful not to let the maid know that you want to test her. For example, if you want to know whether the maid is going to steal or be greedy for small profits, you can pretend to forget to leave copper coins on the table, and secretly remember how many copper coins there are. A day or half a day later, go to the table alone to see if the copper coins are still there, or if a few are missing. If it is intact, this maid is honest. If it is gone or a few are missing, you can know that this maid is dishonest.

After working for a month, if this maid is indeed loyal, thrifty, and can continue to work, then you can relax your precautions, and you do not have to pay attention and strictly supervise her all the time. Within the possible range, you can also entrust part of the work to her completely, such as buying vegetables, cooking, and preparing meals, and let her do everything. She will definitely do it in an orderly manner, and there will be no profiteering or reporting less. Because people have a sense of self-esteem. If they gain the trust of others, their self-esteem is satisfied, and they will definitely work wholeheartedly, especially those with simple minds. Aren't there many old servants who are respectful to their masters, loyal to their duties, and willing to sacrifice themselves to serve their masters?

The housewife's attitude towards the maid should be kind and dignified, so that she feels that you are both approachable and awe-inspiring. Do not speak too commandingly, but mix some ordinary conversation into the commanding style, because speaking in a commanding style will cause unpleasant feelings in the listener, and doing things will be reluctant.

It is inevitable for a person to make mistakes. When a maid does something wrong, what should we do? I think it is best not to scold her, or even beat her. We must first ask the reason for the mistake. If it is unintentional, then there is no need to scold her, just carefully tell her to be careful in the future.

Do not be too harsh on maids. Do not put on the airs of a master, and do not divide the boundaries between master and servant too strictly, treating her as a slave. Rice should be given to her according to her appetite, and the side dishes should not be too meager. Do not arbitrarily shout and send her around. She should be given time to rest every day, after she has finished what she should do. She should be given adequate sleep every day, and unless there are special circumstances, do not make her sleep too late. She should have a small portion of time each day to do her own private affairs—such as tailoring clothes for herself, her children, and her husband, making shoes for her children, or going out to visit relatives and friends.

Do not change servants often, because changing new people often is not only a waste of money—matchmaking fees—but also causes great losses in spirit. When a new maid comes in, how much energy and effort do you have to spend to train her and test her. If she is changed after one or two months, isn't this energy and effort wasted?

There is one point that the housewife must pay the most attention to, that is, do not let the maid know your weaknesses, because cunning

Continued on page 5

Page 22

Page 23

maids will use your weaknesses to satisfy her desires. For example, a housewife who likes to play mahjong, and spends nine and a half days out of ten playing mahjong, the maid will use this weakness to pull "partners" for the mistress every day. In this way, she not only pleases the master, but also has a lot of "extra money"—tips—coming in every day, and can also take the opportunity to joke and slack off arbitrarily when the mistress has no time to take care of the household affairs. A weak, indecisive housewife, if the maid knows her weakness, the maid will take independent action and overstep her authority.

There is also a point, that is, the housewife should not collude with the maid to cheat, and regard the maid as a "confidante." This is most likely to develop the maid's habit of being domineering. For example, a housewife who likes to gamble, but is afraid of being questioned by her husband, she is afraid that the maid will tell her husband, so she uses money to bribe the maid, telling her not to tell the master, and even borrows money from the maid when she lacks gambling money, or asks the maid to pawn items. The first time it is a command style, the second time it is a discussion style, and the third time it becomes a pleading style. In this way, the maid's arrogance is greatly increased. She not only despises the housewife, but also gradually teaches and coerces the housewife. And the housewife, at this time, not only dares not offend her, but also has to contact her, win her favor, and rely on her. So this maid becomes your strategist, advisor, and also your chronic disease.

Sunday Literary Society

Nature and Characters in Literature 202

— Xirong

How can artistic creations be described to be moving? This requires effort in technique. Describing scenery is one of the crucial factors in literary works. To depict nature, one must have a faithful attitude to observe it. The author needs to cultivate a habit of loving nature, and as the master of nature, must never be a servant commanded by it.

The depiction of nature can be divided into three aspects: outlining, describing mood, and describing color:

Literature is also close to painting. Only when people feel as if they are in a painting after reading it can the ability of literature be fully utilized. In the Romantic era, literary techniques often focused on mesoscopic descriptions. Therefore, the works at that time mostly drew materials from the description of trivial matters around the author and often adopted a first-person perspective. However, the huge waves of literary trends have surged to the other shore of new realism. The author's subjective position should not be revealed in the work. It is necessary to penetrate the inner layer of life with an objective attitude, discover its beauty and ugliness, and present it nakedly to the reader, which is progress. Therefore, the natural description in literary works should also be described objectively and meticulously, just like painting. This is called "realism," which is an advancement in landscape painting techniques.

How to record and arrange natural scenery? This is what we must discuss first:

1. Central Point Although the scenery of nature is very complex, a central point can be selected, focusing on the depiction of this central point, while treating other parts as a foil. There is an old saying called "setting off the moon with clouds." The central point should be the moon, and the writing of the clouds is only for the mission of setting off the moon. For example, in Zhu Ziqing's "Lotus Pond Moonlight," he mentioned tall shrubs, faint shadows of willows, vague distant mountains, and scattered streetlights, but what we feel after reading it is only "the freshness of the moonlight." Why is this? Because the central point of description in that article is the "moon."

2. Background Arrangement In addition to the central point, there must be foreground and background, just like painting. It would be too monotonous to paint a lonely village house. Adding a few green willows next to the house is the foreground arrangement. Adding vague distant mountains behind the house is the background arrangement. A picture of a village house constructed in this way will feel perfect and harmonious. However, the color of this background arrangement should not be too rich. Generally, the central point is the richest, the foreground is second, and the background is the last.

For a deep description of scenery, in addition to the outline, one must also rely on a deep, keen perception. Perception is emotional, so the description of "mood" is also necessary. The same bright moon hangs in the sky. To a happy person, the "round, bright moon" further increases infinite joy, but to a melancholic person, the "desolate moonlight" will make one unbearable sad. Why does the same moon evoke such a wide range of emotions? This is because the evoked moods are different. Lu Yin's description of the beauty of Penglai mentions "a detached, otherworldly feeling" and "another kind of secluded interest," which are examples of describing mood.

Also, the color of nature is often related to time. The light has brightness, darkness, intensity, and weakness, and the colors expressed by nature are also different. A clear sky presents a blue color, giving people a sense of relaxation and pleasure; a cloudy sky presents a gray color, giving people a sense of dullness and depression. Those who are good at writing about nature focus on paying attention to these ever-changing colors, so that the entire text reveals different emotions such as excitement, peace, shock, lightness, and purity in the colors.

Next, we want to talk about the creation of characters in literature. Mr. Yu Dafu said: The events in novels are all performed by people, and characters are naturally the most important elements in novels. Based on this understanding, we must devote our greatest efforts to the creation of characters. Lu Xun's "The True Story of Ah Q" not only laid the foundation for the trend of the Chinese literary world, but also the Ah Q he created has become a typical representation of Chinese farmers. This is a good example.

Although people's personalities, habits, behaviors, and thoughts are different, no matter how great a character is, they cannot escape the restrictions of time and space. The influence of time is the "era," and the influence of space is the "social environment" and "natural environment."

First, the environment of time—for example, Confucius was born in the late Zhou Dynasty Spring and Autumn period. The era at that time was one of respecting kings and valuing ritual education. Even with Confucius's wisdom, he could not jump out of that circle. Therefore, criticizing his thoughts with the modern eyes of the twentieth century is naturally a mismatch. Marx was born at a time when the industrial revolution, the factory system, and the rise of capitalism were taking place, which made it possible for the brewing of socialism and the theory of surplus value. Rather than being amazed at Marx's innate greatness, it is better to say that Marx was actually dominated by the spirit of the times.

Second, the limitation of space—the limitation of space can be divided into the limitation of the social environment and the limitation of the natural environment. No one can escape the influence of the artificial environment such as social customs, political systems, and economic background at that time; Mozi was born in a society during the Warring States period where mutual killings were extremely severe, and politicians were engaged in diplomacy and war all day long, so he had the theory of universal love of "regarding the country of others as one's own country, regarding the family of others as one's own family, and regarding the body of others as one's own body." Similarly, no one can escape the influence of the natural environment: northerners are mostly bold and unrestrained, southerners are mostly gentle and weak, people in mountain valleys are mostly stubborn and narrow-minded, people living by the sea are mostly leisurely and romantic, people living in rural villages are mostly honest and simple, and people living in cities are mostly frivolous and flighty. These are all restricted by the natural environment.

When creating characters and expressing their thoughts, behaviors, and emotions, the above-mentioned time, society, and nature should be used as the background, and their personality and psychology should be depicted.

Personal characteristics are the unique qualities of a certain person, and they are individual. If a similar type cannot be found among others besides this person, it is considered personality. Flaubert said: There are no two identical stones or two identical leaves in the world. Everything has its own personality. If you cannot find its personality, you cannot describe the thing. Therefore, the description of characters also needs to express personality. The reason why "Dream of the Red Chamber" has become the swan song of Chinese chapter novels is because Mr. Cao Xueqin was able to grasp the personality characteristics of each character in the Grand View Garden and do his best to depict them. It is said that the author of "Water Margin" once drew pictures of the portraits of the 108 heroes in advance, and gazed at them day and night to ponder them, so the 108 characters he portrayed became distinct personalities.

Yu Dafu's "On Novels" has a passage about characters: "The characters in works are mostly typical characters, so they are more interesting than the characters in actual society, and most of them have the characteristics of a class or a society. For example, Don Quixote is a representative of dreamers, Hamlet is a representative of skeptics, and Tartufe (a character in Molière's comedy) is a representative of hypocrites. The reason why the characters of writers can make most readers feel interested in the characters of the author is precisely because they have this kind of Typical traits of Characteristics. However, when this kind of representative characteristic is abstracted too much, it is easy to lose the individuality of the characters and become characters in fables, such as Christam Hypocrite in Bunyan's "The Pilgrim's Progress," or become a Caricature, making readers unable to feel the overflowing sense of reality. This level is the most difficult point for novelists to create characters, and it is also the biggest turning point for success or failure." These theories are really the motto of novelists.

Literary Works

Diary from the Back Building (1) 203

— Shuyu

September 8, 1930

I am a poor salaried worker, and cannot afford a day of idleness; but now I have been unemployed for nearly two months, and this unemployment, like the previous one, is gradually destroying the spirit and resources that I had painstakingly restored!

Writing a diary seems to be a special enjoyment only for the leisure class. When I have a job, I am always busy all day long and have no time to hold a pen; taking advantage of the current loneliness and boredom, sorrow and depression, I can just be close to this little booklet and pour out every drop of my pain to it, accumulating it inside, making it my own shadow, to share the heavy burden of all my misfortunes.

In the modern deformed society where time is money, even if we put aside the saying that "an inch of time is worth an inch of gold," it is not profitable for a person to be too idle. Recently, I have been so idle that I feel bored - but this is obviously forced and violates my psychology. In fact, I am not idle at all - I am lonely and depressed all day long. Therefore, when I started writing this diary, I felt that there was nothing to write about.

Life is really too empty! Besides the two major events of eating and sleeping, there is nothing else to fill its content, and I have no intention of reading. As my spirit becomes increasingly depressed and my mind gradually declines and becomes lazy, I have hardly been aware of space and time in the past two months. I confine myself to a small, cage-like room all day long, and I don't want to run anywhere, can't run, or even dare to peek out from the window at the prosperous city built of gold and white jade. I don't remember the days and hours much, and I have never touched things like calendars. Really, playing with things like signing in at the office - no! Now that I think about it, that was a pleasure - I haven't been doing it for a long time. I no longer pay attention to which day is Sunday to rest, or which days are not Sunday and should be working; I pay no attention to the passage of time, the passing of years, or the change of seasons. If it weren't for the landlady asking me yesterday, "So, when are you moving in? Is tomorrow okay? Tomorrow is the 8th," I really wouldn't know what day it is today! It seemed like I had heard someone mention "September," but "8th" was a bit vague.

The landlady's slightly rectangular and flat face is really the most suitable, a living calendar that cannot be bought with money. She reported the date to me very accurately. I promised her that I would move to her place on the 14th.

Remembering the days and cherishing time is really a very stupid thing for me. Recently, I have definitely felt more tired of this difficult life than before. I only hope that time will pass quickly, to shorten my useless life that is only busy for living every day. I am suffering from "life sickness," and "death" is a specific medicine! This is a new invention of mine in modern medicine.
